Second Premise: Defining Being in Place and Its Dilemma
Second premise defining 'being in place' sensorily and the dilemma for God

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the sensory definition of 'being in place' and the logical dilemma it creates if applied to God.

Core Idea
Being in a place means being pointable; for God, that leads to an impossible choice.

This passage presents the second premise in a series of rational arguments for God's transcendence. The author defines what it means for something to be 'in a place' in a sensory sense. We will see that this definition forces a dilemma: if God were in a place, He would have to be either touching the world or separate from it, both of which are problematic. This lays the groundwork for rejecting divine corporeality.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the literal translation. Let the author's definition and dilemma sink in.
2
Identify the definition of 'being in place'
Notice that the author defines being characterized by place and direction as the ability to be pointed to sensorily as 'here' or 'there'. This is a clear, empirical definition.
The phrase 'إشارة حسية' is key.
3
Note the two possibilities
The passage states that if God were in place in this sense, then either He is in contact with the world (مماس) or separate from it (مجانب). There is no third option given.
These are the only two rational possibilities.
4
Understand why the third option is unintelligible
The author declares that a being being pointed to sensorily while being neither in contact nor separate is unintelligible (غير معقول). Reflect on why this is logically impossible.
This rejection is based on the nature of spatial occupancy.
5
Consider the broader argument
Think about how this dilemma sets up a proof for God's transcendence: since both options are incompatible with divinity, God cannot be in place at all.
This premise leads to the conclusion that God is not spatial.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المقدمة الثانية : أن مرادنا بقولنا إن الشيء الفلاني مختص بالمكان والجهة أنه يمكن أن يشار إليه إشارة حسية بأنه هنا أو هناك، ولا شك أن العالم في المكان والجهة بهذا التفسير، فلو كان الباري تعالى مختصا بالمكان والجهة بهذا التفسير لم يخل الحال من أحد أمرين، وهو إما أن يكون الباري تعالى مماسًا للعالم أو مجانبًا له، فأما أن يكون الباري تعالى مشارًا إليه بحسب الحس بأنه هنا أو هناك مع أنه لا يكون مماسًا للعالم ولا محاذيًا له فهذا غير معقول.
The Second Premise: Our meaning when we say that a certain thing is characterized by place and direction is that it can be pointed to by a sensory indication as being here or there. And there is no doubt that the world is in place and direction according to this interpretation. So if the Exalted Creator were characterized by place and direction according to this interpretation, the situation would not be free from one of two things: either the Exalted Creator is in contact with the world or is separate from it. As for the Exalted Creator being pointed to sensorily as here or there while He is neither in contact with the world nor contiguous with it, that is unintelligible.
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This passage is the second premise (al-muqaddima al-thāniya) in a series of premises leading to a proof of God's transcendence. The author defines what it means for something to be 'characterized by place and direction' (mukhtaṣṣ bi al-makān wa al-jiha): it means that an external observer can point to it sensorily indicating 'it is here' or 'it is there'. The world clearly fits this definition. If God were also characterized by place and direction in this sense, then one of two things must be true: either God is in direct contact (mumāss) with the world, or He is separate (mujānib) from it. The third possibility—that God could be pointed to sensorily as being somewhere while being neither in contact nor separate—is deemed unintelligible (ghayr ma'qūl). This sets up a dilemma: any notion of God being in a place forces an unacceptable consequence.

Key Terms

إشارة حسية

محاذي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The premise claims that God cannot be pointed to at all.
Correction: The premise does not say that; it defines what being in a place means (sensorily pointable) and then shows that if God were in a place in that sense, it leads to an unacceptable dilemma. The conclusion that God is not in place is derived from the dilemma, not from an inability to point.

C) It must be in contact with something else
D) It must be separate from everything

Key Takeaway
To be in a place means to be pointable sensorily, and if God were in a place, He would have to be either touching or separate from the world, both of which contradict His transcendence.

Refuting the Karramiyyah View of Direction
Razi refutes the Karramiyyah view by analyzing its three logical possibilities.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three possible interpretations of the Karramiyyah claim that God is in a direction, and the logical refutation of the infinite distance view.

Core Idea
The Karramiyyah view of God being above leads to logical absurdities.

Imam Razi here refutes the Karramiyyah sect who claimed that Allah is located in the direction of above. He categorizes their view into three interpretations and shows that the most sophisticated version—infinite distance—is either a denial of direction or meaningless. This argument reinforces the mainstream Sunni position that Allah is transcendent beyond place and direction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three interpretations
Read the passage carefully and list the three ways the Karramiyyah view can be understood according to logical division.
The first two involve contact or finite separation; the third involves infinite separation.
2
Analyze the infinite distance view
Focus on the third interpretation held by the Haysamiyyah. Understand the author's claim that it either negates direction or is unintelligible.
Infinite distance between two bounded points is contradictory.
3
Understand the logical problem
Grasp why the author argues that infinite distance between the Throne and Allah would be bounded by the two, making it finite. This is a contradiction.
This refutes the Karramiyyah position without rejecting direction per se.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المقدمة الثالثة : ذهب السواد الأعظم من العقلاء إلى أنه تعالى منزه في وجوده عن المكان والحيز والجهة وقالت الكرامية : إنه مختص بجهة فوق، وهذا القول بحسب القسمة العقلية يحتمل ثلاثة أوجه : أحدها: أن يقال : إنه مماس للعرش. وثانيها : أنه مباين للعرش يبعد متناه وأكثر طوائف الكرامية قائلون بأحد هذين القولين. وثالثها: أن يقال : إنه تعالى مباين للعرش ببعد لا نهاية له، وهذا هو قول الهيضمية واعلم أن هذا القول إما أن يكون نفيا لكونه تعالى في الجهة أو يكون قولا غير معقول، وذلك لأنه إذا كان العالم في أحد الجانبين وذات الباري تعالى في الجانب الآخر كان البعد بينهما محصورًا، والقول بأن ما لا نهاية له محصور بين حاصرين لا يقوله من يفهم معاني هذه الألفاظ.
The Third Premise: The great majority of rational people hold that He, exalted, is transcendent in His existence above place, space, and direction. And the Karramiyyah said: He is characterized by the direction of above. And this statement, according to rational division, admits of three aspects: One of them: that He is said to be in contact with the Throne. The second: that He is separate from the Throne at a finite distance, and most sects of the Karramiyyah affirm one of these two statements. And the third: that He, exalted, is separate from the Throne at an infinite distance, and this is the statement of the Haysamiyyah. And know that this statement either is a negation of His being in direction or is an unintelligible statement. That is because if the world is on one side and the essence of the Exalted Creator is on the other side, then the distance between them would be bounded. And the statement that what is infinite is confined between two bounds is not said by one who understands the meanings of these words.
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This passage is the third premise (al-muqaddima al-thālitha). It begins by noting the majority view of rational people that God is transcendent above place, space, and direction. It then presents the Karramiyyah view that God is characterized by the 'direction of above' (jihata fawq). According to rational classification, this view has three possible interpretations: (1) God is in physical contact (mumāss) with the Throne, (2) God is separate from the Throne at a finite distance (mubāyin li-l-'arsh bi-bu'd mutanāh), or (3) God is separate at an infinite distance (bi-bu'd lā nihāya lahu). Most Karramiyyah adopt one of the first two. The third, held by the Haysamiyyah, is examined: it either amounts to a negation of God being in direction (if infinite distance means no bounded direction) or is unintelligible. The author argues that if the world is on one side and God is on the opposite side, the distance between them must be finite, i.e., bounded by the Throne and God. Claiming that an infinite distance is enclosed between two bounds is a contradiction in terms. Thus the Karramiyyah position is refuted.

Key Terms

مماس

هيضمية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Karramiyyah view that God is above is logically coherent.
Correction: The third interpretation of infinite distance leads to a contradiction: infinite distance cannot be bounded by two finite objects.

Checkpoint

B) It is unintelligible
C) It is the majority view
D) It contradicts the Throne

Key Takeaway
The claim that Allah is at an infinite distance from the Throne is logically self-contradictory, thus refuting the Karramiyyah position.

Razi's argument forces us to choose: either the Karramiyyah view is false, or we accept a logical absurdity. Are there areas of your faith where you prefer a comforting but logically flawed idea over a demanding truth? Commit today to seeking truth even if it makes you uncomfortable.

First Proof: Everything in a Direction is Either an Atom or a Composite Body
First rational proof that anything in a direction is either atom or body, both insufficient for God.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why anything that exists in a direction must be either indivisible (an atom) or divisible (a composite body), and how both are incompatible with God's transcendence.

Core Idea
God cannot be in a direction because that would reduce Him to an atom or a body.

In this lesson, we examine the first rational proof that God is not located in any direction. The argument is a simple dichotomy: anything that occupies a direction is either indivisible (like a theoretical atom) or divisible (a composite body). Both possibilities are unworthy of God. The opponents themselves agree that God is beyond such attributes.

Guided Path
1
Understand the proof's structure
The proof is a logical dichotomy. The author first states the two possible cases for anything in a direction: indivisible or divisible.
Notice the Arabic phrase 'إما أن يكون' which signals a dichotomy.
2
Analyze the first branch: indivisible atom
If it is indivisible yet sensorily perceivable, it would be like the indivisible atom, which is extremely small and lowly. The opponents concede that God is not like that.
The atom (جوهر فرد) is the smallest unit in kalam ontology.
3
Analyze the second branch: composite body
If it is divisible, then it is a composite body, which implies parts and composition—God is exalted above that.
Composition implies contingency and need for components.
4
Draw the conclusion
Since both possibilities are unfit for God, the only coherent position is that God is not in a direction.
This proof establishes divine transcendence from physical location.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذ قد لخصنا هذه المقدمات فلنرجع إلى ذكر الدلائل الحجة الأولى : كل ما كان في جهة فإما أن يكون غير محتمل للقسمة وإما أن يكون محتملا للقسمة، فإن لم يكن محتملا للقسمة، مع أنه مشار إليه بحسب الحس، كان في الصغر والحقرة كالجوهر الفرد والخصوم وافقوا على أنه يجب تنزيه الله عن هذه الصفة، وأما إن كان مشارًا إليه مع أنه محتمل للقسمة كان جسما مركبا تعالى الله عن ذلك.
And since we have summarized these premises, let us return to mentioning the proofs. The first proof: Everything that is in a direction is either not susceptible to division or is susceptible to division. If it is not susceptible to division, while being pointed to sensorily, it would be in smallness and lowliness like the indivisible atom, and the opponents agree that God must be transcended above this attribute. And if it is pointed to while being susceptible to division, it would be a composite body—God is exalted above that.
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This passage is the first proof (al-hujja al-ūlā) after summarizing the premises. The argument is a dichotomy: anything that exists in a direction is either indivisible (i.e., an atom, jawhar fard) or divisible (a composite body, jism murakkab). If it is indivisible and yet can be pointed to sensorily, it would be extremely small and insignificant, like the atom. All opponents agree that God must be transcendent above such lowliness. If it is divisible and pointed to, then it would be a composite body, which implies contingency and composition—also impossible for God. Therefore, God cannot be in a direction. This proof succinctly refutes any notion of God having a location by showing that it leads to absurd consequences that contradict divine majesty.

Key Terms

قسمة
جوهر فرد
جسم مركب
تنزيه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The proof denies that God can be perceived or pointed to at all.
Correction: The proof only denies that God is located in a direction; it does not deny that God can be known or pointed to in a metaphorical sense.

Checkpoint

B) A composite body
C) A spiritual substance
D) An abstraction

Key Takeaway
The first proof against God being in a direction uses a simple either/or: anything in a direction is either an indivisible atom or a composite body, both of which are incompatible with God's transcendence.

First Preliminary: The Intellect Does Not Find It Impossible to Conceive of Something Without Place
Razi argues that the impossibility of a spaceless being is not self-evident using the example of numbers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the impossibility of a spaceless being is not a self-evident truth and why rational proof is required.

Core Idea
The intellect can conceive beings without place; their impossibility is not obvious.

This passage is the first preliminary in Imam Razi's theological work. He aims to show that the belief that Allah cannot be without place is not a self-evident truth; rather, it requires proof. Through the example of numbers, he demonstrates that the intellect can conceive essences without location.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation. Note how Razi uses the example of numbers to illustrate his point.
The first word 'الاثنين' might be a continuation from a previous page; focus on the main argument.
2
Identify the key example
Razi says the intellect perceives numbers (e.g., two) and their essences without attributing any place or magnitude to them. Understand this example.
3
Follow the conclusion
Razi concludes that since the intellect can conceive of numbers without location, it can also conceive of a being without place. Therefore, the impossibility of such a being is not self-evident.
This sets up the need for rational arguments about Allah's attributes.
4
Reflect on the broader significance
Consider why this preliminary is important for theology: it clears the ground for reasoned discussion about divine transcendence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الاثنين وكذا مسمى مراتب الأعداد أمور يدركها العقل ولا يمكنه أن يحكم على ماهية الواحد من حيث إنه واحد بأن مكانه هو موضع كذا ومقداره هو مقدار كذا، بل يعقل العقل هذه الماهيات ولا يعتبر معها البتة لا مقدارًا ولا شكلاً، ولا حيزا فثبت هذه الوجوه أن العقل من حيث إنه هو لا يستبعد تصور معقول حال ما لا له مكانا ولا جهة ولا قدرًا ولا شكلاً ، فثبت أن العلم بامتناع هذا الموجود ليس من العلوم البديهية.
"The two [or: Monday] and likewise the named ranks of numbers are things that the intellect (العقل) perceives, but it cannot judge concerning the essence (ماهية) of the one insofar as it is one that its place is such and such a location and its magnitude is such and such a magnitude. Rather the intellect cognizes these essences and does not consider along with them at all any magnitude, shape, or location. So it is established by these aspects that the intellect, in itself, does not deem impossible the conception of a mental object (معقول) that has no place, direction, magnitude, or shape. Thus it is established that knowledge of the impossibility of this being is not among the self-evident sciences (العلوم البديهية)."
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This passage is a preliminary premise (muqaddima). Imam Razi argues that the impossibility of a being without space and direction is not self-evident. He uses the example of numbers and mathematical entities: the intellect understands the essence of numbers (e.g., two) without attributing to them any location or magnitude. Similarly, the intellect can conceive of a being free from these attributes. Therefore, one cannot simply claim it is obviously impossible and must provide proof. This sets up the need for rational arguments.

The possibility of a spaceless being is rationally conceivable; its impossibility is not self-evident but requires proof.

4 min
The Impossibility of God Being in a Location
Razi defines location and argues against God being in it via a dichotomy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Razi's definition of being in a location and why the alternatives lead to an impossibility if applied to God.

Core Idea
God cannot be in a location because it would force either contact or separation, both impossible.

Razi begins his second preliminary by defining what it means for an object to be in a place. He then applies this definition to the Creator, showing that if God were in a location, He would have to be either touching the world or separate from it—but the third possibility is unintelligible. This lays the groundwork for proving God's transcendence above space.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definition of location
Read Razi's definition of being in a location: it means being capable of sensory indication as 'here' or 'there'. The world fits this definition.
This is a key conceptual move: location is tied to sensory perception.
2
Apply the dichotomy to God
If God were in a location, there are only two logical possibilities: He touches the world (mumass) or is separate from it (mujanib). Recognize that these are the only options.
This dichotomy is exhaustive; no third option exists.
3
Reject the third possibility
The idea that God could be sensorily pointed to without being either touching or separate is dismissed as unintelligible (غير معقول). Understand why this is impossible.
This sets up the proof that God cannot be in a location.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المقدمة الثانية : أن مرادنا بقولنا إن الشيء الفلاني مختص بالمكان والجهة أنه يمكن أن يشار إليه إشارة حسية بأنه هنا أو هناك، ولا شك أن العالم في المكان والجهة بهذا التفسير، فلو كان الباري تعالى مختصا بالمكان والجهة بهذا التفسير لم يخل الحال من أحد أمرين، وهو إما أن يكون الباري تعالى مماسًا للعالم أو مجانبًا له، فأما أن يكون الباري تعالى مشارًا إليه بحسب الحس بأنه هنا أو هناك مع أنه لا يكون مماسًا للعالم ولا محاذيًا له فهذا غير معقول.
"The second preliminary: That our meaning in our statement 'such-and-such a thing is specific to place and direction' is that it can be pointed to by a sensory indication (إشارة حسية) as being 'here' or 'there'. There is no doubt that the world is in place and direction according to this interpretation. So if the Exalted Creator (الباري تعالى) were specific to place and direction by this interpretation, the situation would not be free from one of two matters: either the Exalted Creator would be in contact (مماسًا) with the world or separate (مجانبًا) from it. As for the possibility that the Exalted Creator is pointed to by sense as being 'here' or 'there' while not being in contact with the world nor juxtaposed to it—this is unintelligible (غير معقول)."
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This passage is the second preliminary. Razi first defines what he means by an object being in a location: it must be perceivable by the senses as being in a specific place. The world (i.e., the universe) clearly fits this definition. Then he presents a dichotomy: if God were in a location, He would either be touching the world (mumass) or separate from it (mujanib). There is no third possibility. The idea that God could be perceptible in a location without being either touching or separate is dismissed as unintelligible. This sets up the argument that since God cannot touch the world (due to His transcendence) and cannot be separate from it (as that would imply a finite distance, which will be refuted later), it is impossible for Him to be in a location.

Key Terms
مكان
جهة
إشارة حسية
مماس
مجانب
غير معقول

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think God could be in a location without being touching or separate from the world, as a vague 'presence'.
Correction: Razi argues that being in a location necessarily entails either contact or separation; the alternative is logically impossible.

Checkpoint
According to Razi's definition, what does it mean for something to be in a place?
A) It exists.
B) It can be seen.
C) It can be pointed to sensorily as here or there.
D) It is measurable.

Key Takeaway
Razi establishes that being in a location implies sensory indication and forces a dichotomy of contact or separation, making it impossible for God to be in a location.

If Allah cannot be in a location, then He is not limited by space. How does that change the way you think about His closeness to you? What practical step can you take to feel that closeness without placing Him in a location?

First Proof: The Argument from Comparison with the Throne
Imam Razi's tripartite argument against direction using the Throne

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Imam Razi's logical argument that affirming a direction for Allah leads to composition and divisibility, which are impossible for the Divine.

Core Idea
Affirming a direction for Allah forces composition, which is impossible for the Divine.

In this passage, Imam Razi presents a foundational proof against the belief that Allah is located in a direction. He uses the Throne as a concrete reference to show that any spatial relation inevitably leads to composition and division. This argument is critical for establishing Allah's absolute transcendence beyond space and direction.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation to grasp the overall argument.
Notice the dense logical structure.
2
Identify the secret (sirr)
Razi begins by stating that his school agrees: whoever affirms Allah in space and direction must admit composition.
This is the core claim to be proven.
3
Understand the tripartite division
Razi divides the possibility of being above the Throne into three cases: greater, equal, or smaller. Each case leads to composition or absurdity.
This is a classic qiyas al-ta'seem.
4
Consider the alternative argument
Razi notes that if one accepts that every extended object is divisible, then any direction itself implies divisibility, strengthening the case.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
The conclusion is that any direction entails impossible attributes for Allah, so Allah must be transcendent beyond direction.
This is a decisive proof in Islamic theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسألة الثامنة من الأجزاء والأبعاض وحينئذ يرجع الكلام إلى المسألة الأولى، ولهذا السر اتفق أصحابنا على أن كل من أثبت الله تعالى في الحيز والجهة لا بد وأن يعترف بكونه مركبا من الأجزاء والأبعاض. واعلم أن أصحابنا عبروا عن هذه الدلالة بأن قالوا : لو كان في جهة فوق لكان إما أن يكون أكبر من العرش أو مساويًا له أو أصغر منه فإن كان أكبر من العرش كان القدر المساوي منه العرش مغايرا للقدر الفاضل منه من العرش، فيكون مركبا من الأجزاء والأبعاض، وإن كان مساويًا للعرش وثبت أن العرش منقسم من الأجزاء والأبعاض كان مساويًا له في المقدار منقسما، مركبًا من الأجزاء والأبعاض، وإن كان أصغر من العرش فإما أن يكون قد بلغ في الصغر إلى أن كان مساويًا للجوهر الفرد، والجزء الذي لا يتجزأ ، فيكون في غاية الصغر والحقارة - وجل ربنا عن باتفاق العقلاء - وإما أن يكون أكبر من الجوهر الفرد، ويعود القول بالتركيب والقسمة. ذلك واعلم أن على قول من يقول : كل متحيز فهو قابل للقسمة أبدا لا نحتاج إلى ذكر هذا التقسيم بل نقول : كل ما كان مشارًا إليه بحسب الحس فإنه لا بد وأن يتميز يمينه عن يساره وقدامه عن ورائه وفوقه عن تحته فيكون منقسمًا مركبا من الأجزاء والأبعاض، وذلك مما بينا امتناعه في المسألة السابقة.
The eighth issue: concerning parts and fragments, and then the discussion returns to the first issue. For this secret our companions agreed that whoever affirms Allah Most High in space and direction must inevitably admit that He is composed of parts and fragments. Know that our companions expressed this indication by saying: If He were in an upward direction, then either He is greater than the Throne, or equal to it, or smaller than it. If He is greater than the Throne, then the part of Him equal to the Throne is different from the part of Him exceeding the Throne, so He would be composed of parts and fragments. If He is equal to the Throne and it is established that the Throne is divisible into parts and fragments, then He would be equal to it in magnitude, divisible, composed of parts and fragments. If He is smaller than the Throne, then either He has reached such smallness as to be equal to the indivisible atom and the part that cannot be divided, and so He would be in the utmost smallness and lowliness—far exalted is our Lord by the consensus of the intelligent—or He is larger than the indivisible atom, and the claim of composition and division returns. That is so. Know that according to the one who says: every atom is perpetually divisible, we do not need to mention this division, but rather we say: everything that is perceptibly pointed to must necessarily have its right distinguished from its left, its front from its back, and its above from its below, so it is divisible, composed of parts and fragments, and that is what we demonstrated as impossible in the preceding issue.
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage is a proof (hujja) from Imam Razi against the claim that Allah is in a direction or location. He begins by stating the eighth issue (al-mas'ala al-thamina) concerning parts and fragments, noting that this discussion returns to the first issue. He then reveals the secret (sirr) that his school (ashabuna) agrees: whoever affirms Allah in space (hayyiz) and direction (jiha) must admit composition (tarkib) from parts and fragments, which is impossible. The proof itself is a tripartite division: if Allah were above ('above' meaning in an upward direction relative to the Throne), then He must be either larger than, equal to, or smaller than the Throne. If larger, the part equal to the Throne differs from the extra part, so He is composed. If equal, since the Throne is divisible, He too would be divisible and composed. If smaller, either He equals the indivisible atom (jawhar fard) which is extremely small and lowly—exalted is Allah above that—or He is larger than the atom, and composition returns. He then notes that if one accepts that every atom is divisible, the division is unnecessary; instead, any object perceptible by sense must have distinguishable right/left, front/back, top/bottom, implying divisibility and composition, which was already shown impossible in the previous issue.

Key Terms
جهة (jiha)
حيز (hayyiz)
تركيب (tarkib)
أجزاء وأبعاض (ajza' wa-aba'd)
عرش ('arsh)
جوهر فرد (jawhar fard)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Being above the Throne does not require spatial composition because Allah is not physical.
Correction: Razi argues that any spatial relation, even conceptual, forces a distinction of parts in the entity, implying composition. Thus, affirming direction entails composition.

Checkpoint
What does Imam Razi conclude about anyone who affirms that Allah is in a direction (jiha)?
A) They must admit that Allah is composed of parts and fragments.
B) They must believe Allah is above the Throne.
C) They must affirm the indivisible atom.
D) They must deny the existence of the Throne.

Key Takeaway
Imam Razi demonstrates that affirming a direction for Allah logically entails composition, which is impossible for the Creator, thereby establishing His transcendence beyond space and direction.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you imagine Allah, do you ever subconsciously picture Him as being 'up there'? How does Razi's argument challenge that subconscious assumption, and what are you going to do to train your mind to think of Allah without any direction?
?
The passage says that if Allah were smaller than the Throne, He would be in the utmost smallness and lowliness. Have you ever thought about Allah's greatness in a way that actually diminishes it, by confining Him to a place? What concrete steps can you take today to replace that mental image with one of absolute transcendence?
?
Razi's proof forces a logical conclusion. But does your heart accept it fully, or do you find yourself struggling because you feel closer to Allah when you imagine Him 'above'? How can you reconcile the necessity of transcendence with the desire for closeness?

Second Proof: The Impossibility of Allah Being Perceptible
Imam Razi provides a logical proof that Allah cannot be perceptibly pointed to because that would entail finitude and origination.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Imam Razi argues that anything perceptibly pointed to must be finite and originated, and therefore cannot apply to Allah.

Core Idea
What can be pointed to is limited; Allah has no limits.

Imam Razi presents his second proof against the idea that Allah is in a direction. He argues that anything that can be pointed to by the senses must have spatial dimensions, making it finite and contingent. Through a detailed logical analysis, he shows that applying such attributes to Allah leads to absurdities. This lesson unpacks his reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the main premise
Start by reading the initial statement: 'Everything that is perceptibly pointed to must have its right distinguished from its left, so it is finite from all sides.' Understand that this is the foundation of the proof.
2
Examine the first reason
Razi gives two reasons for the premise. The first is a reference to a known proof about the finitude of dimensions in bodies. Accept this as established.
The text says 'there is no doubt in it' despite an OCR issue.
3
Analyze the second reason
The second reason is a detailed argument by contradiction. Follow how Razi considers both possibilities of infinity (all sides or some sides) and shows they lead to absurdities.
Pay attention to the subcases when infinite from some sides.
4
Understand the conclusion
After establishing finitude, Razi concludes that the finite thing must be originated (needs a specifier) and that it cannot be above all existents. Thus, being perceptibly pointed to is impossible for Allah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثانية : كل ما كان مشارًا إليه بحسب الحس فإنه لا بد وأن يتميز يمينه عن يساره، فهو متناه من جميع الجوانب، وكل ما كان متناهيا من جميع الجوانب فهو محدث وإنما قلنا : إن كل ما كان مشارًا إليه بحسب الحس فهو متناه من جميع الجوانب لوجهين : الأول : البرهان المذكور في مسألة حدوث الأجسام على تناهي الأبعاد، وذلك ريب فيها. الثاني: هو أنه تعالى لو كان غير متناه لكان إما أن يكون غير متناه من جميع الجوانب أو بعض الجوانب، لا جائز أن يكون غير متناه من جميع الجوانب؛ لأن على هذا التقدير يلزم أن يكون العالم ساريًا في ذات الله تعالى وحالا فيه، ويلزم أن تكون ذاته مخالطة للقاذورات - تعالى الله عن هذه المقالة، وعن هذا الوهم والخيال - ولا جائز أن يقال إنه غير متناه من بعض الجهات دون البعض، وذلك لأن الجانب ذاته إما أن يكون مساويًا للجانب الآخر - الذي هو غير متناه في الحقيقة والماهية - وإما أن لا يكونا متساويين فإن كان الأول فكل شيئين متساويين من جميع الوجوه، فكل ما يصح على أحدهما يصح على الآخر، فيلزم أن يقال : الجانب الذي هو غير متناه يصح أن ينقلب متناهيا، والجانب الذي هو متناه يصح أن ينقلب غير متناه فيكون الفصل والوصل والتركيب والتفريق جائزا على ذات الله تعالى فيفتقر ذلك التأليف إلى مؤلف، وذلك التركيب إلى مركب وذلك على خالق العالم محال ممتنع ، وأما إن كان الجانب المتناهي مخالفًا في الماهية للجانب الذي هو غير متناه، فكل ذات كانت مركبة من أجزاء مختلفة في الماهية والطبيعة، فلا بد وأن ينتهي في ذلك التركيب إلى أجزاء يكون كل واحد منها في نفسه بسيطا خاليا من التركيب فالجزء الواحد من تلك الأجزاء البسيطة لا بد وأن يماس بيمينه شيئًا، وبيساره شيئًا آخر، ذلك الذي ماسه يمكن أن يماسه بيساره وبالضد وإذا كان ذلك جائزا كان التفرق على تلك الأجزاء جائزا فحينئذ يكون التأليف والتركيب والتفرق جائزا على تلك الأجزاء، ومتى كان الأمر كذلك افتقر تأليفها وتركيبها إلى مؤلف ومركب، وكل ذلك محال. فثبت بما ذكرنا أنه تعالى لو كان مشارًا إليه بحسب الحس لكان متناهيا من جميع الجوانب ونقول : إنه متى كان كذلك وجب أن يكون محدثًا، وذلك لأن كل ما كان متناهيا من جميع الجوانب كان وجوده أزيد مما وجد، أو أنقص مما وجد جائزا ، وإذا كان كذلك كان اختصاصه بذلك القدر المعين من الجائزات مفتقرًا إلى مخصص ومقدر، وذلك على خالق العالم محال. وأيضًا إذا كان متناهيًا من كل الجوانب لم يكن فوق كل الموجودات لأن فوقه أمكنة خالية عنه فلم يكن فوق الكل، والخصم ينكر ذلك ولا يرضاه، فثبت أن كونه تعالى مشارًا إليه بحسب الحس محال.
The second proof: Everything that is perceptibly pointed to must necessarily have its right distinguished from its left, so it is finite from all sides. And everything that is finite from all sides is originated. We say: Everything that is perceptibly pointed to is finite from all sides for two reasons. The first: the demonstration mentioned in the issue of the origination of bodies concerning the finitude of dimensions, and there is no doubt in it. The second: If He Most High were infinite, then either He would be infinite from all sides or from some sides. It is not possible that He be infinite from all sides, because on this assumption it would follow that the world pervades the essence of Allah Most High and is inherent in it, and it would follow that His essence is mixed with filth—exalted is Allah above this statement, and above this imagination and fantasy. And it is not possible to say that He is infinite from some sides without others, because the side itself is either equal to the other side—which is actually infinite in reality and essence—or they are not equal. If the first, then any two things equal in all respects, whatever is true of one is true of the other, so it would follow that the side which is infinite could become finite, and the side which is finite could become infinite, so separation and conjunction, composition and division would be possible in the essence of Allah Most High, and that composition would need a composer, and that combination would need a combiner, and that is impossible and impossible regarding the Creator of the world. And if the finite side is different in essence from the infinite side, then every essence composed of parts differing in essence and nature must ultimately lead in that composition to parts each of which is in itself simple and free from composition. Then the single part of those simple parts must necessarily touch with its right something and with its left something else; what it touches could be touched by its left or the opposite. If that is possible, then division among those parts is possible. Then composition, combination, and division would be possible among those parts. Whenever that is the case, their composition and combination would need a composer and a combiner, and all that is impossible. So it is established by what we have mentioned that if He Most High were perceptibly pointed to, He would be finite from all sides. And we say: whenever that is the case, He must be originated, because everything finite from all sides, its existence being more than what exists or less than what exists is possible. If that is so, then its specification with that particular amount among possibilities needs a specifier and an estimator, and that is impossible regarding the Creator of the world. Also, if He were finite from all sides, He would not be above all existents because above Him there are spaces empty of Him, so He would not be above everything, and the adversary denies that and is not satisfied with it. So it is established that His being perceptibly pointed to is impossible.
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage is the second proof (al-hujja al-thaniya) from Imam Razi against the claim that Allah is in a direction. He begins by stating the premise: anything perceptibly pointed to (musharun ilayhi bil-hiss) must have distinct right and left sides, implying it is finite from all sides. Everything finite from all sides is originated (muhdath). He then gives two reasons why perceptibility implies finitude. The first reason references the proof from the issue of the origination of bodies (mas'alat huduth al-ajsam) concerning the finitude of dimensions, which he says is beyond doubt. The second reason is a detailed argument by contradiction: if Allah were infinite, He would have to be infinite from all sides or from some sides. If infinite from all sides, the world would pervade His essence and mingle with filth, which is impossible. If infinite from some sides, he examines two cases: either the finite side is equal in essence to the infinite side, or they are different. If equal, whatever applies to one applies to the other, so the infinite could become finite and vice versa, implying composition and need for a composer. If different, the composition must resolve into simple parts that touch and separate, again requiring a composer. Thus, finitude necessitates origination because a finite thing could have been larger or smaller, requiring a specifier (mukhassis). Additionally, if Allah were finite, He would not be above all, as there would be empty spaces above Him. Hence, being perceptibly pointed to is impossible for Allah.

Key Terms
مشار إليه بحسب الحس (musharun ilayhi bil-hiss)
متناه (mutanahi)
محدث (muhdath)
تناهي الأبعاد (tanahi al-ab'ad)
غير متناه (ghayr mutanahi)
مخصص (mukhassis)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think finitude only applies to physical objects, but Razi argues anything perceptible must be finite, and Allah cannot be perceptible.
Correction: Razi's argument is not about physicality but about the logical implications of being perceptibly pointed to. He shows that such an attribute entails finitude and origination, which are incompatible with Allah.

Checkpoint
According to the second proof, what does being 'perceptibly pointed to' (musharun ilayhi bil-hiss) imply?
A) It implies being infinite in some directions.
B) It implies being composite and needing a composer.
C) It implies being finite from all sides and thus originated.
D) It implies being equal to the Throne.

Key Takeaway
Allah cannot be perceptibly pointed to because that would imply He is finite and originated, which contradicts His divinity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you catch yourself trying to 'picture' Allah in your mind, even subconsciously, what does that reveal about your understanding of His transcendence? What will you do the moment such a thought arises, starting today?
?
This proof shows that anything finite requires a specifier — a cause that determines its specific qualities. In what areas of your life do you still act as if you are self-sufficient, not needing Allah's specification and guidance? Write one concrete step to entrust that area to Him.
?
If you truly internalized that Allah cannot be pointed to or contained by any direction, how would it change your attitude towards the places where you worship, your body, or your concept of 'nearness' to Him? What is one change you commit to making?

Divine Transcendence
beginner

Third Proof: Location Implies Motion or Incapacity
Imam Razi presents a dilemma regarding Allah's place.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical dilemma Imam Razi uses to prove that Allah cannot be in a place or direction.

Core Idea
If Allah were in a place, He would be either mutable or deficient—both impossible.

This lesson presents the third of Imam Razi's proofs against the idea that Allah occupies a location. He constructs a dilemma: if Allah were in a place, He must either be able to leave it or not. Both options lead to absurdities—motion implying createdness, or paralysis implying deficiency. Follow along as Razi uses this logical tool to defend divine transcendence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Note the flow of the argument.
2
Identify the two horns of the dilemma
Find the 'either...or' structure. The first horn is that leaving the place is possible; the second is that it is impossible.
Both lead to something incompatible with Allah's nature.
3
Examine the consequence of each horn
If leaving is possible, it implies motion and rest, which indicate createdness. If impossible, it implies deficiency like paralysis.
Refer to the commentary for clarification.
4
Understand the underlying principle
Anything subject to motion and rest is originated (muhdath). This is a key axiom in kalam.
This principle is established in the discussion of the origination of bodies.
5
Connect to divine transcendence
Since both horns lead to impossibilities, the premise—that Allah is in a place—is false. This reinforces tanzih.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثالثة : لو كان ذاته مختصا بمكان وجهة لكان إما أن يخرج منها أو لا يصح، فإن صح لزم كونه محلا للحركة والسكون، وكل ما كان كذلك كان محدثًا على ما بيناه في مسألة حدوث الأجسام، وإن تعذر عليه الخروج منها كان كالزمن المقعد العاجز عن الحركة وذلك صفة نقص، وهو على الله تعالى محال.
The third proof: If His essence were specific to a place and direction, then either He could leave it or it could not be valid. If it is valid, then it follows that He is subject to motion and rest, and everything that is such is originated, as we have explained in the issue of the origination of bodies. If leaving it is impossible for Him, then He would be like a paralyzed person unable to move, and that is a quality of deficiency, and it is impossible for Allah Most High.
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This passage is the third proof (al-hujja al-thalitha) from Imam Razi against the claim that Allah is in a location or direction. He presents a dilemma: if Allah's essence were specific to a place and direction (makān wa jiha), then either He can leave that place or He cannot. If He can leave, then He would be subject to motion (haraka) and rest (sukūn), and anything subject to motion and rest is originated (muhdath), as established in the issue of the origination of bodies. If He cannot leave, then He would be like a paralyzed person ('ajiz 'an al-haraka), which is a quality of deficiency (naqs), and such is impossible for Allah. Thus, both horns of the dilemma lead to an impossibility, proving that Allah cannot be in a place or direction.

Key Terms
مكان (makan)
جهة (jiha)
حركة (haraka)
سكون (sukun)
محدث (muhdath)
نقص (naqs)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that being in a place does not necessarily entail motion, so Razi's dilemma is flawed.
Correction: Razi shows that if Allah could leave, motion is possible (and rest is its absence), both indicating createdness. If He could not leave, that itself is a deficiency. Thus the dilemma stands.

Checkpoint
What does Imam Razi say about the possibility of Allah leaving the place if He were in one?
A) It is impossible, so Allah must be deficient.
B) If possible, it implies motion and origin; if not possible, it implies deficiency.
C) It is necessary for Allah to leave, proving His power.
D) There is no dilemma; Allah is above all places.

Key Takeaway
Allah's transcendence above place is proven by a logical dilemma: location would necessitate either motion (implying creation) or paralysis (implying deficiency), both impossible for Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever catch yourself imagining Allah as being 'up there' in the sky, as if confined to a place? How can this proof reshape your mental image of Allah and deepen your worship? Will you consciously train your mind to think of Allah as beyond all spatial limitations?
?
The proof says that if Allah could not leave a place, He would be like a paralyzed person. In what areas of your life do you subconsciously act as if Allah is 'stuck' or unable to help you due to your circumstances? How can you remind yourself daily that Allah is absolutely free and capable?
?
Imam Razi links motion to being created. Do you ever attribute change or new events to Allah in a way that implies He 'moves' or changes? How can you ensure your belief in Allah's actions remains consistent with His transcendence, avoiding any hint of physicality?

The Dilemma of Two Sides: Equality in Quiddity
Imam Razi presents the first case of his dilemma: equal sides lead to composition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first part of Imam Razi's argument: if Allah were perceptible by senses, He would have two sides, and if those sides are equal in quiddity, composition would follow, which is impossible.

Core Idea
If two sides are equal, then the infinite could become finite and composition becomes unavoidable.

Imam Razi begins his proof against divine location by considering a hypothetical body with two sides: one finite and one infinite. He proposes two possibilities: either these sides are equal in quiddity or they are not. In this lesson, we examine the first case — equality — and see how it leads to an impossible consequence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage, noting the key terms: متساويين (equal), ماهية (quiddity), متناه (finite), غير متناه (non-finite).
2
Understand the principle of equality
If two things are equal in all respects, everything valid for one is valid for the other. Apply this to the two sides.
3
Connect to impossibility
If the infinite side can become finite and vice versa, then composition and separation become possible for Allah's essence, requiring a creator. That is impossible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والماهية - وإما أن لا يكونا متساويين فإن كان الأول فكل شيئين متساويين من جميع الوجوه، فكل ما يصح على أحدهما يصح على الآخر، فيلزم أن يقال : الجانب الذي أن ينقلب متناهيا، والجانب الذي هو متناه يصح أن ينقلب غير متناه فيكون الفصل والوصل والتركيب والتفريق جائزا على ذات الله تعالى فيفتقر ذلك التأليف إلى مؤلف، وذلك التركيب إلى مركب وذلك على خالق العالم محال ممتنع ، وأما إن كان الجانب المتناهي مخالفًا في الماهية للجانب الذي هو غير متناه، فكل ذات كانت مركبة من أجزاء مختلفة في الماهية والطبيعة، فلا بد وأن ينتهي في ذلك التركيب إلى أجزاء يكون كل واحد منها في نفسه بسيطا خاليا من التركيب فالجزء الواحد من تلك الأجزاء البسيطة لا بد وأن يماس بيمينه شيئًا، وبيساره شيئًا آخر، ذلك الذي ماسه يمكن أن يماسه بيساره وبالضد وإذا كان ذلك جائزا كان التفرق على تلك الأجزاء جائزا فحينئذ يكون التأليف والتركيب والتفرق جائزا على تلك الأجزاء، ومتى كان الأمر كذلك افتقر تأليفها وتركيبها إلى مؤلف ومركب، وكل ذلك محال.

فثبت بما ذكرنا أنه تعالى لو كان مشارًا إليه بحسب الحس لكان متناهيا من جميع الجوانب ونقول : إنه متى كان كذلك وجب أن يكون محدثًا، وذلك لأن كل ما كان متناهيا من جميع الجوانب كان وجوده أزيد مما وجد، أو أنقص مما وجد جائزا ، وإذا كان كذلك كان اختصاصه بذلك القدر المعين من الجائزات مفتقرًا إلى مخصص ومقدر، وذلك على خالق العالم محال.

وأيضًا إذا كان متناهيًا من كل الجوانب لم يكن فوق كل الموجودات لأن فوقه أمكنة خالية عنه، فلم يكن فوق الكل، والخصم ينكر ذلك ولا يرضاه، فثبت أن كونه تعالى مشارًا إليه بحسب الحس محال.
And the quiddity—or that they are not equal. If the first [case], then every two things equal in all respects, everything valid for one is valid for the other. So it follows that it is said: the side that is [non-finite] can become finite, and the side that is finite can become non-finite. Then separation, conjunction, composition, and division become permissible for Allah's essence. So that composition requires a composer, and that combination requires a combiner, and that is impossible and prohibited for the Creator of the world. And if the finite side differs in quiddity from the side that is non-finite, then every essence composed of parts differing in quiddity and nature must eventually in that composition end in parts each of which is in itself simple, devoid of composition. So the single part of those simple parts must touch something with its right and with its left another thing. That which it touched can be touched by its left or the opposite. If that is permissible, then separation upon those parts is permissible. Then composition, combination, and separation are permissible upon those parts. And when that is the case, their composition and combination depend on a composer and combiner, and all that is impossible.

So it is established by what we mentioned that if He (Exalted) were perceptible by sense, He would be finite from all sides. And we say: whenever that is the case, He must be originated. That is because everything finite from all sides, its existence being more than what existed or less than what existed is permissible. And if that is so, its specification with that particular amount among permissibles depends on a specifier and determiner, and that is impossible for the Creator of the world.

Also, if He is finite from all sides, He is not above all existents because above Him there are empty spaces, so He is not above all. And the opponent denies that and is not pleased with it. So it is established that His being perceptible by sense is impossible.
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This passage is a proof (burhan) that Allah cannot be perceptible by the senses, which would imply being in a place and direction. The argument proceeds by considering a hypothetical body with two sides: one finite and one infinite. The argument examines two possibilities: either the two sides are equal in quiddity or they are not equal. If they are equal in all respects, then whatever applies to one applies to the other, so the infinite side could become finite and vice versa, implying that separation, conjunction, composition, and division are possible for Allah's essence, which would require a composer—impossible for the Creator. If they are not equal (different in quiddity), then the compound essence must ultimately decompose into simple parts that are in contact with others, allowing separation and composition, again requiring a composer. Both cases lead to impossibility. From this, Imam Razi concludes that if Allah were perceptible by sense, He would be finite from all sides. He then argues that anything finite is contingent because its specific measure requires a specifier, and that would make Allah originated, which is impossible. Additionally, a finite being cannot be above all existents since there would be empty spaces above it, contradicting the opponent's claim. Thus, the idea that Allah is perceptible by sense and located in a place is false.

Key Terms
متناه
غير متناه
ماهية
متساويين
تركيب
تأليف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that equality of sides is harmless and does not lead to imperfection.
Correction: The argument shows that equality leads to interchangeability, which implies change and composition, incompatible with Allah's perfection.

Checkpoint
What follows from the assumption that the two sides are equal in all respects?
A) The sides remain distinct and unchanging.
B) The infinite side can become finite and the finite can become infinite.
C) The sides become one.
D) Nothing changes.

Key Takeaway
The first case shows that equality of sides leads to the possibility of composition, which is impossible for the Creator.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think about Allah, do you ever imagine Him as having parts or being subject to change? How does this argument expose the hidden flaw in such mental images, and what must you actively do to purify your concept of Allah from any hint of composition?
?
If the very possibility of composition in Allah is impossible, what does that mean for your own reliance on logical categories when describing Him? Are you willing to accept that your mind cannot fully comprehend His transcendence, even when arguments seem clear?
?
This dilemma shows that any change in Allah's essence would imply dependence. Examine your own heart: do you ever feel that Allah changes towards you based on your actions? How can you anchor your trust in His unchanging nature despite your fluctuating states?

The Second Case: Sides Differ in Quiddity
Imam Razi presents the second case of his dilemma: differing quiddities lead to composition via simple parts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Imam Razi's argument that if the two sides differ in quiddity, the compound essence must decompose into simple parts, leading to composition and dependence on a composer.

Core Idea
Different quiddities force decomposition into simple parts, requiring a composer.

After showing the impossibility of equal sides, Imam Razi considers the second possibility: that the two sides differ in quiddity. He argues that any compound composed of different parts must ultimately consist of simple, indivisible parts. These simple parts, by their nature, must touch other parts, making separation and composition possible. This again requires a composer, which is impossible for Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic text for the second case, focusing on the concepts of 'different in quiddity', 'simple parts', and 'touching'.
2
Trace the decomposition argument
If parts differ in quiddity, they cannot be simple. They must decompose until reaching simple parts. Those simple parts touch others, which introduces the possibility of separation.
3
Conclude the impossibility
Since separation and composition are possible, a composer is needed. That is impossible for Allah, so this second possibility is also false.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والماهية - وإما أن لا يكونا متساويين فإن كان الأول فكل شيئين متساويين من جميع الوجوه، فكل ما يصح على أحدهما يصح على الآخر، فيلزم أن يقال : الجانب الذي أن ينقلب متناهيا، والجانب الذي هو متناه يصح أن ينقلب غير متناه فيكون الفصل والوصل والتركيب والتفريق جائزا على ذات الله تعالى فيفتقر ذلك التأليف إلى مؤلف، وذلك التركيب إلى مركب وذلك على خالق العالم محال ممتنع ، وأما إن كان الجانب المتناهي مخالفًا في الماهية للجانب الذي هو غير متناه، فكل ذات كانت مركبة من أجزاء مختلفة في الماهية والطبيعة، فلا بد وأن ينتهي في ذلك التركيب إلى أجزاء يكون كل واحد منها في نفسه بسيطا خاليا من التركيب فالجزء الواحد من تلك الأجزاء البسيطة لا بد وأن يماس بيمينه شيئًا، وبيساره شيئًا آخر، ذلك الذي ماسه يمكن أن يماسه بيساره وبالضد وإذا كان ذلك جائزا كان التفرق على تلك الأجزاء جائزا فحينئذ يكون التأليف والتركيب والتفرق جائزا على تلك الأجزاء، ومتى كان الأمر كذلك افتقر تأليفها وتركيبها إلى مؤلف ومركب، وكل ذلك محال.

?

?

?

Conclusion: Finitude Implies Contingency and Not Being Above All
Imam Razi presents two final arguments: finitude implies contingency and not being above all.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Razi concludes that if Allah were perceptible by senses (and thus finite), He would be contingent and not above all existents, which is impossible.

Core Idea
Finitude demands a specifier; being finite also means not being above all.

Having established that perceptibility by senses implies finitude, Imam Razi now draws two further consequences. First, anything finite must be contingent because its specific measure requires a specifier. Second, a finite being cannot be above all existents, as there would be empty spaces above it. Both conclusions contradict the nature of Allah, proving that He cannot be perceptible by senses.

Guided Path
1
Read the concluding passage
Read the Arabic from 'فثبت' to the end. Identify the two separate arguments: one about contingency, one about being above all.
2
Understand the contingency argument
If something is finite from all sides, its size could have been more or less. That it has a specific size means it needs a specifier (mukhassis), which shows it is originated (muhdath).
3
Understand the 'above all' argument
If it is finite, there are empty spaces above it, so it is not above all existents. This contradicts the opponent who claims Allah is above everything.
4
Realize the final conclusion
Both consequences are impossible for Allah, so the premise that He is perceptible by senses is false.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

What does the argument claim about a finite being's size?

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you imagine Allah, do you unconsciously picture a being in a specific direction? How does Razi's argument challenge that assumption, and what can you do to purify your concept of Allah today?
?
The argument shows that anything finite depends on a specifier. In your life, are you treating anything (status, relationships, possessions) as if it were self-sufficient, forgetting that everything besides Allah is contingent and dependent? What would it look like to rely only on Allah as the only necessary being?
?
Razi proves that being finite means not being above all. In your daily mindset, do you act as if you are 'above' certain people or situations? How does recognizing Allah's absolute transcendence and your own finitude change your attitude towards others?

The Impossibility of Allah Being in a Place
A disjunctive proof (hujja) showing the absurdity of Allah being in a place.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Allah's transcendence requires that He is not confined to any place or direction, and how the impossibility of both leaving and not leaving a place proves this.

Core Idea
If Allah were in a place, He would either be subject to change or be deficient — both impossible.

Imam Razi presents a crisp logical argument against the notion that Allah occupies a place. By examining the two possibilities that follow from such a claim — either Allah could leave that place or not — he shows both lead to contradictions with divine perfection. This argument reinforces the Islamic tenet of Allah's transcendence (tanzih) above physical constraints.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Sanusi uses a very compressed style here.
2
Identify the dichotomy
The passage presents two possibilities when a thing is in a place: either it can leave or not. Find these two branches in the text.
3
Analyze the first branch
If Allah could leave the place, He would undergo motion and rest — properties of originated bodies. That would imply He is created, impossible for Allah.
This depends on the earlier proof of the origination of bodies.
4
Analyze the second branch
If Allah could not leave the place, He would be like a paralyzed person, which is an attribute of deficiency. Deficiency is impossible for Allah.
5
Draw the conclusion
Since both options are absurd, the original assumption (that Allah is in a place) must be false. Allah is transcendent, free from spatial limitations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثالثة : لو كان ذاته مختصا بمكان وجهة لكان إما أن يخرج منها أو لا يصح، فإن صح لزم كونه محلا للحركة والسكون، وكل ما كان كذلك كان محدثًا على ما بيناه في مسألة حدوث الأجسام، وإن تعذر عليه الخروج منها كان كالزمن المقعد العاجز عن الحركة وذلك صفة نقص، وهو على الله تعالى محال.
The third proof: If His essence were specific to a place and direction, then either He could leave it or not. If [leaving] is possible, then He would be a locus of motion and stillness, and everything that is so is originated, as we explained in the issue of the origination of bodies. And if leaving is impossible for Him, then He would be like a paralyzed person incapable of movement, and that is an attribute of deficiency, and it is impossible for Allah (Exalted).
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This passage is a short proof (hujja) demonstrating the impossibility of Allah being in a place. Imam Razi presents a dichotomy: if Allah were in a place, either He can leave that place or He cannot. If He can leave, then He would be subject to motion and rest, which are characteristics of originated bodies, making Him originated—impossible for Allah. If He cannot leave, then He is like a paralyzed person unable to move, which is a deficiency—also impossible for Allah. Both options are absurd, so the premise that Allah is in a place is false.

Key Terms

جهة
حركة
سكون
محدث
نقص

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some anthropomorphists claim Allah is literally 'above' the Throne, implying He is in a direction or place.
Correction: This argument shows that if Allah were in a place, He would either be subject to change (motion/rest) or be incapacitated — both impossible. Thus, while Allah is 'above' in rank, He is not spatially located.

Checkpoint
What does the third argument show if Allah cannot leave His place?
A) He is omnipotent
B) He is like a paralyzed person
C) He is eternal
D) He is independent of place

Key Takeaway
Allah is not confined to any place or direction; both motion and incapacity are impossible for Him.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you make du'a facing the qibla, do you ever feel that Allah is 'in front' of you? How does this lesson challenge that feeling? What will you do today to internalize that Allah is not spatially bound, yet closer to you than your jugular vein?
?
Think about a time you felt distant from Allah because you thought He was 'far away'. How did that feeling affect your faith? Now that you know Allah cannot be confined to any place, will you change how you remind yourself of His nearness? Commit to one verbal reminder (e.g., saying 'Allah is with me') when you feel distant.
?
The proof shows that attributing place to Allah implies either change or deficiency. Have you ever, even unconsciously, thought of Allah as limited by time or space? What does that reveal about the images you hold of Allah? Will you actively purify your conception of Allah by reflecting on this argument daily for a week?

6 min
The Dilemma of Place: Existent or Non-Existent
Imam Razi presents a dilemma: if the place is existent, it implies pre-eternity of bodies and dependency; if non-existent, it cannot contain an existent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why attributing a place to Allah leads to absurd consequences, whether that place is considered existent or non-existent.

Core Idea
If Allah were in a place, the place would either rival Him in eternity or be unable to contain Him.

Imam Razi begins by presenting a powerful dilemma. If the opponent claims Allah is in a place, that place must either be something that exists or something that does not. Both options lead to conclusions that are impossible for Allah. This lesson walks through each possibility and shows why they fail.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice how Imam Razi sets up the dilemma.
2
Analyze the first horn
If the place is existent, it would be eternal with Allah, implying pre-eternity of bodies and making Allah dependent on place.
3
Analyze the second horn
If the place is non-existent (pure negation), it has no specificity and cannot contain an existent.
4
See the conclusion
Both options are impossible, so the claim that Allah is in a place is false.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الرابعة وهو أنه تعالى لو كان في مكان وجهة فهذا المكان الذي حكم الخصم بأنه تعالى فيه إما أن يكون موجودًا أو معدوماً، فإن كان موجودًا فالباري تعالى مختص بالمكان والجهة من الأزل إلى الأبد، فحينئذ كان ذلك المكان موجودًا مع الله في الأزل، وهو محال؛ لأن ذلك المكان لما كان موجودًا وكان قابلا للقسمة كان ذلك عين الجسم، فكان هذا قولا بقدم الأجسام.

وأيضًا: المكان لا يفتقر في وجوده إلى المتمكن لأن الخلاء جائز بالاتفاق، وأما الباري تعالى فإنه عند الخصم يمتنع وجوده في غير الحيز والجهة، فعلى هذا يكون الباري تعالى مفتقرا في وجوده وتحققه إلى وجود المكان، ووجود المكان غنيا عنه، فكان تعالى على هذا التقدير ممكنا لذاته مفتقرًا إلى غيره، وكان المكان واجبًا لذاته غنيًا عن غيره، فكان المكان أولى بأن يكون هو الإله سبحانه وتعالى والإله أولى بأن يكون العبد، وكل ذلك ساقط من القول.

وأما إن قيل : بأن المكان الذي حكم الخصم بكونه تعالى حالا فيه معدوم صرف ونفي محض، فهذا محال من القول ؛ لأن النفي المحض والعدم الصرف لا تخصص له ولا تعين ،له وما كان كذلك استحال القول بحصول الموجود فيه، فثبت أن القول بحصول الباري تعالى في المكان محال.

فإن قيل : فهذا الإشكال بعينه وارد في كون الجسم في المكان،
قلنا : المراد بكون الجسم في المكان كونه بحيث يمكن الإشارة إلى كل واحد من جوانبه، بأنه غير الآخر، وبأنه متصل به ومماس له ويرجع حاصل كونه في المكان والجهة إلى مقداره واتصال بعض أجزائه بالبعض فإن أردتم بقولكم : " الله تعالى في المكان هذا المعنى كان هذا تصريحًا بكونه تعالى مركبا من الأجزاء والأبعاض، وحينئذ يرجع الكلام إلى المسألة الأولى.
The fourth proof: That if He (Exalted) were in a place and direction, then this place which the opponent claims He is in is either existent or non-existent. If it is existent, then the Creator (Exalted) is specific to the place and direction from eternity to eternity. Then that place would be existent with Allah in eternity, and that is impossible; because that place, being existent and divisible, would be exactly a body, so this would be a statement of the pre-eternity of bodies.

Also: The place does not depend in its existence on the occupant, because empty space is permissible by agreement. As for the Creator (Exalted), according to the opponent, His existence in other than space and direction is impossible. So on this basis, the Creator (Exalted) would depend in His existence and realization on the existence of place, while the existence of place is independent of Him. Thus, on this estimation, He would be possible in essence, dependent on another, while place would be necessary in essence, independent of another. Then place would be more deserving to be the God (Glorified and Exalted), and God would be more deserving to be the servant. All of that is worthless speech.

And if it is said that the place which the opponent claims He is in is pure non-existence and mere negation, then this is impossible speech; because pure negation and mere non-existence have no specification and no determination. And whatever is like that, it is impossible to say that an existent occurs in it. So it is established that the statement that the Creator (Exalted) occurs in a place is impossible.

If it is said: This very objection applies to the body being in a place.
We say: What is meant by the body being in place is that it is such that one can point to each of its sides, that it is other than the other, and that it is connected and contiguous to it. The essence of its being in place and direction reduces to its magnitude and the connection of some of its parts to others. If you intend by your statement 'Allah is in a place' this meaning, then this is an explicit declaration that He is composed of parts and fragments, and then the discussion returns to the first issue.
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This passage is a proof (hujja) with an objection and answer. Imam Razi presents the fourth argument: if Allah were in a place, that place is either existent or non-existent. If it is existent, then it would coexist with Allah from eternity, making it an eternal body—this implies belief in the pre-eternity of bodies, which is false. Moreover, the place does not need the occupant, but Allah would need the place (according to the opponent), making Allah contingent and place necessary—absurd. If the place is nonexistent (pure negation), then it has no specification and cannot contain an existent. Thus both options fail.

Then an objection is raised: this same problem applies to a body being in a place. Imam Razi answers: The body's being in place means that it has magnitude and parts that are connected and contiguous; pointing to its sides is possible. If the opponent means this by 'Allah is in a place', then they are explicitly saying Allah has parts, which returns to the first problem (composition). So the objection is neutralized.

Key Terms
مكان
موجود
معدوم
قدم الأجسام
خلاء
ممكن
واجب
نفي محض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that a non-existent 'place' could still be a conceptual container, but the argument shows that pure negation cannot have any specificity.
Correction: Non-existence is not a thing; it cannot be a location. The opponent's claim that Allah is in a 'non-existent' place is self-contradictory.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if the place is existent, what absurd consequence follows?
A) The place would be non-existent.
B) The place would be eternal and divisible, implying pre-eternity of bodies.
C) Allah would be independent of place.
D) The place would be dependent on Allah.

Key Takeaway
The dilemma shows that claiming Allah is in a place leads to absurdities whether the place exists or not.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever habitually imagined Allah as being 'up there' or 'in the heavens' as if He occupies a place? What does this argument reveal about the hidden assumptions in your heart regarding Allah's location? Are you willing to uproot those mental images and affirm that He is not confined to any place, even if it feels uncomfortable?
?
The argument shows that if place were existent and eternal, it would rival Allah's eternity. Search your life: are there any 'places' (roles, possessions, relationships) that you treat as if they are eternal or independent of Allah? How does this argument call you to dethrone them from your heart?
?
If pure non-existence cannot contain an existent, then what does it mean for you to 'find' Allah? Does this argument push you to realize that Allah is not found by locating Him spatially, but by knowing Him through His attributes? How will you change your approach to seeking nearness to Allah after learning this?

Objection and Clarification: What Does 'Body in Place' Mean?
Imam Razi answers the objection that the same problem applies to bodies, clarifying that 'body in place' means magnitude and parts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Razi responds to the objection that the same dilemma applies to bodies, by clarifying the meaning of 'being in a place'.

Core Idea
The body's 'in place' means magnitude and connection, not simple containment.

An opponent may object: 'Your dilemma applies equally to any body being in a place. If that is impossible, then bodies cannot be in places either!' Imam Razi answers by clarifying what 'being in a place' actually means for a body: it refers to magnitude, pointing to sides, and connection of parts. This meaning cannot apply to Allah without implying composition, which is already rejected.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Read the objection carefully: 'This very objection applies to the body being in a place.'
2
Understand the answer
Imam Razi explains that for a body, 'being in a place' means having magnitude and connected parts, such that you can point to its sides.
3
Apply to Allah
If this meaning is applied to Allah, it implies He has parts and composition, which is the first issue.
4
See the resolution
Thus the objection does not refute the argument; it only shows that the opponent's claim leads to even worse consequences.

Source Text

The fourth proof: That if He (Exalted) were in a place and direction, then this place which the opponent claims He is in is either existent or non-existent. Then place would be more deserving to be the God (Glorified and Exalted), and God would be more deserving to be the servant. All of that is worthless speech.

Fifth Argument: Spaces Either Equal or Different in Quiddity
Razi presents a dilemma on spaces being equal or different in quiddity, leading to absurdity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Imam Razi's fifth argument against Allah being in a space, showing that both possibilities (spaces equal or different in quiddity) lead to absurdity.

Core Idea
Allah cannot occupy space because any placement requires a specifier or implies multiple eternal entities.

This lesson examines Imam Razi's fifth proof from the 'Al-Arba'in', which argues that Allah cannot be located in any space or direction. The proof presents a dilemma: either all spaces are equal in quiddity or they are different. Both options lead to conclusions that are incompatible with Allah's pre-eternity and oneness. As you read the passage, notice how Razi sets up the two branches and begins to derive their implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
The passage is cut off at the end due to a page break.
2
Identify the two branches
The passage presents two possibilities: spaces equal in quiddity, or spaces different in quiddity. Find where each is mentioned and note the initial reasoning for each.
The first branch is discussed more fully; the second is introduced but not completed.
3
Understand the argument for equal spaces
If spaces are equal and Allah can be in one, then He can be in any, so His actual location requires a specifier. That specifier would be eternal, which is impossible.
This refutes the idea that Allah could occupy any space at all.
4
Consider the argument for different spaces
If spaces are different, each has a unique property that determines whether Allah can be in it. But then spaces become eternal self-subsisting entities, implying multiple eternals.
The argument is cut off, but the intended conclusion is that this is also impossible.
5
Reflect on the overall point
Both branches lead to impossibility, so Allah cannot be in any space or direction. This reinforces divine transcendence (tanzih).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الخامسة : الأحياز والجهات إما أن تكون متساوية في الماهية أو مختلفى في الماهية، فإن كان الأول لزم من صحة اختصاص الباري تعالى ببعض الأحياز صحة اختصاصه بسائر الأحياز بدلا عن ذلك الحيز، وإذا كان حصوله في كل واحد منها بدلًا عن الآخر أمرًا جائزا كان حصوله في بعض تلك الأحياز أمرًا جائزا، فيفتقر ذلك الاختصاص إلى المخصص وهو على القديم محال، وأما إن قلنا بأن الأحياز مختلفة في الماهية والحقيقة فلعل خاصية بعض تلك الأحياز اقتضى حصول ذات الله تعالى فيه وخاصية بعضها اقتضى امتناع حصول الله فيه.

فنقول : هذه الأحياز أشياء متباينة بالعدد ومتباينة بالماهية ولكل واحد منها خاصة معينة وصفة معينة، فهي أشياء موجودة قائمة بأنفسها موجودة في الأزل، فإذا
The fifth proof: Spaces and directions are either equal in quiddity or different in quiddity. If the first [case], then the validity of the Creator (Exalted) being specific to some spaces entails the validity of His being specific to all other spaces instead of that space. And if His occurrence in each one of them instead of the other is permissible, then His occurrence in some of those spaces is permissible, so that specification requires a specifier, and that is impossible for the Pre-eternal. And if we say that spaces are different in quiddity and reality, perhaps the property of some of those spaces necessitates the occurrence of Allah's essence in it, and the property of some necessitates the impossibility of Allah occurring in it.

So we say: These spaces are things distinct in number and distinct in quiddity, and each one has a specific property and specific attribute. They are existent things subsisting by themselves, existent in eternity. So if...
Source pages p. 112

Commentary
This passage is a proof (hujja) that is incomplete due to the page break. Imam Razi presents the fifth argument: spaces and directions (places) are either equal in quiddity or different. If they are equal, then if it is valid for Allah to be in one, it is valid for Him to be in any, so His specification to a particular space would require a specifier, which is impossible for the Eternal. If spaces are different in quiddity, then each has a specific property, implying they are eternal, self-subsisting entities—this would mean multiple eternal entities, which is also impossible. The argument is cut off, but the implication is that both options lead to absurdity, so Allah cannot be in any space or direction.

Key Terms
أحياز
جهات
ماهية
متساوية
مختلفة
مخصص
قديم
خاصية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Allah can be in a place without being part of it, or that He is in a specific direction like above the throne.
Correction: This argument shows that any placement requires either a specifier (implying a cause for Allah's location) or multiple eternal entities (shirk). Both are impossible, so Allah is beyond space and direction.

Checkpoint
According to the fifth argument, if spaces are equal in quiddity, what follows from Allah being in one space?
A) He must be in all spaces
B) He could be in any space, requiring a specifier
C) Spaces are eternal
D) He is not in any space

Key Takeaway
Both possibilities for the nature of spaces lead to absurdity, so Allah cannot be located in any space or direction.
