Where in your daily life must you now actively seek His presence, knowing He cannot be limited by space? Will you make a habit of remembering Him in your workplace or market, or will you continue to only feel spiritual in 'sacred' spaces?
?
The argument shows that if Allah were in a space, He would either need a specifier (making Him dependent) or share eternity with other entities. Does your heart ever attribute 'luck' or 'chance' to how events unfold? How does this lesson challenge any notion that Allah is subject to circumstances or 'spaces' in your life? Repent from any thought that limits His absolute control.

If spaces are not containers for Allah, then your physical location does not determine His nearness to you. What does this mean for your prayer? Will you now strive for khushu' (attentiveness) in every spot you pray, even if it's a corner of your office? Or will you excuse distraction because 'this isn't a proper prayer space'?

The First Branch: Equal Places Require a Particularizer
Razi presents the first branch of the dilemma: equal places require a particularizer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the assumption that all places are equal in essence leads to the impossibility of God being in a specific place, because it would require a pre-eternal particularizer.

Core Idea
If all places are equal, God's presence in any one requires a chooser—impossible for the Eternal.

Imam Razi presents the fifth proof against the claim that God occupies a direction. This proof is structured as a dilemma. In the first branch, he considers the scenario where all places and directions are equal in their essence. If so, then God's specific location in one place rather than another would need a cause to specify it—a particularizer. But since God is pre-eternal, any such particularizer would also be pre-eternal, creating an impossible chain. Let's examine this argument step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
Read the Arabic passage for the first branch carefully, then the translation. Notice how Razi sets up the conditional.
The passage begins with 'إن كان الأول'.
2
Identify the key logical move
Razi argues that if places are equal, then God's occupation of one place implies the possibility of occupying any other place. That possibility requires a particularizer.
3
Understand why the particularizer is impossible
Since God is pre-eternal, any particularizer would also need to be pre-eternal, leading to an infinite regress or a pre-eternal cause for God's action—both impossible in Islamic theology.
This is the crux of the argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الخامسة : الأحياز والجهات إما أن تكون متساوية في الماهية أو مختلفة في الماهية، فإن كان الأول لزم من صحة اختصاص الباري تعالى ببعض الأحياز صحة اختصاصه بسائر الأحياز بدلا عن ذلك الحيز، وإذا كان حصوله في كل واحد منها بدلًا عن الآخر أمرًا جائزا كان حصوله في بعض تلك الأحياز أمرًا جائزا، فيفتقر ذلك الاختصاص إلى المخصص وهو على القديم محال، وأما إن قلنا بأن الأحياز مختلفة في الماهية والحقيقة فلعل خاصية بعض تلك الأحياز اقتضى حصول ذات الله تعالى فيه وخاصية بعضها اقتضى امتناع حصول الله فيه. فنقول : هذه الأحياز أشياء متباينة بالعدد ومتباينة بالماهية ولكل واحد منها خاصية معينة وصفة معينة، فهي أشياء موجودة قائمة بأنفسها موجودة في الأزل، فإذا كانت هذه الأحياز غير متناهية كان قد وجد مع الله تعالى في الأزل موجودات قائمة بالنفس غير متناهية، وذلك لا يرتضيه المسلم، فثبت أن القول بأن الله تعالى في الجهة محال.
The fifth proof: places (أحياز) and directions (جهات) are either equal in essence or different in essence. If the first, then from the validity of the particularization of the Exalted God to some places follows the validity of His particularization to all other places instead of that place, and if His occurrence in each of them instead of the other is permissible, then His occurrence in some of those places is permissible, so that particularization would need a particularizer (مخصص), and that is impossible regarding the pre-eternal (قديم). And if we say that places are different in essence and reality, perhaps the property of some of those places necessitated the occurrence of God's essence in it, and the property of some necessitated the impossibility of God's occurrence in it. We say: these places are things distinct in number and distinct in essence, each having a specific property and specific attribute, so they are existing things subsisting by themselves, existing in pre-eternity (أزل), so if these places are infinite, then there would have existed with God in pre-eternity infinite self-subsisting existents, and that is not acceptable to a Muslim. So it is established that the statement that God is in a direction is impossible (محال).
Source pages p. 112

Commentary
This passage presents the fifth proof against the claim that God occupies a place or direction. The proof is structured as a dilemma. First branch: if all places and directions are equal in their essence, then God's specific occupation of one place rather than another would require a particularizer or chooser. But since God is pre-eternal, any particularizer would also have to be pre-eternal, leading to an infinite regress or a pre-eternal cause for God's action, which is impossible. Second branch: if places are different in essence, each has a unique property that determines whether God can occupy it. Since places are infinite in number (assuming infinite directions), this would imply the existence of infinite self-subsisting entities co-eternal with God, which is unacceptable in Islam. The conclusion is that God cannot be in any direction.

Key Terms
أحياز
جهات
مخصص
قديم
محال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the first branch, what would God's particularization to a specific place require?
A) A particularizer
B) Divine will
C) The nature of the place
D) Nothing

Key Takeaway
The first branch shows that assuming all places are equal leads to the impossible need for a pre-eternal particularizer.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you imagine God, do you unconsciously picture Him as being 'somewhere' — perhaps above the clouds or in a specific direction? How does this lesson's argument about the impossibility of a particularizer for the Eternal confront that image? ?
If you have ever felt spiritually closer to God in a particular location (like a mosque or a mountain), does that experience contradict the lesson? ?
The argument shows that assuming God is in a place leads to absurdities like an eternal particularizer. Have you ever held onto a belief about God simply because it was familiar or traditional, even if it logically undermined His transcendence? Would you be willing to let go of any mental image of God that accidentally confines Him, no matter how dear it is to you? What would that cost you, and is it worth it?

The Second Branch: Different Places Imply Infinite Co-Eternal Entities
Razi presents the second branch of the dilemma: different places imply infinite co-eternal entities.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the assumption that places are different in essence leads to the unacceptable conclusion of infinite co-eternal entities, thus refuting God being in a direction.

Core Idea
If places differ in essence, each is a unique self-subsisting entity—leading to infinite number co-eternal with God.

Imam Razi continues the fifth proof by considering the second branch of the dilemma: places are different in essence. If so, each place has its own property that either allows or prevents God's presence. However, this would mean that places are existing, self-subsisting entities that were present in pre-eternity alongside God. If there are infinite such places, then infinite co-eternal entities exist with God, which is unacceptable. Let's examine how this seals the argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the second branch passage
Read the Arabic and translation for the second branch. Notice how Razi shifts from the first alternative to the second.
The passage begins with 'وأما إن قلنا'.
2
Understand the implication of different essences
If places have different essences, each has a specific property that determines God's relation to it. This means places are distinct realities.
3
Recognize the problem of infinite co-eternal entities
Since places would have existed in pre-eternity alongside God, if they are infinite in number, that means infinite self-subsisting entities co-existed with God in pre-eternity—a notion rejected in Islam.
This is the core of the impossibility.
4
Conclude the overall proof
Both branches lead to impossibility, so the statement that God is in a direction is impossible.
Razi ends with 'فثبت أن القول بأن الله تعالى في الجهة محال'.

So it is established that the statement that God is in a direction is impossible (محال).

The Sixth Proof: Spherical Earth Denies Direction
Razi presents the sixth proof based on spherical earth to deny Allah's direction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Razi uses the spherical earth and the relativity of 'above' and 'below' to prove that Allah cannot be in a direction or place.

Core Idea
If the earth is round, 'above' is relative; God cannot be in a relative direction.

In this lesson, Razi presents a sophisticated cosmological argument that combines empirical observation with logical reasoning. He first demonstrates that the earth is spherical, then shows that if God were in a fixed direction like 'above', He would be both above and below relative to different observers — a contradiction. This leads to the conclusion that God is beyond place and direction.

Guided Path
1
Read the proof
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice that it starts with a claim (world is a sphere) and then argues from it.
This is a dense argument; read slowly.
2
Understand the lunar eclipse evidence
Razi uses the observation of a lunar eclipse at different longitudes to prove the earth is spherical. How does that work? Think about time zones.
The key is that the same eclipse is seen at different local times, indicating curvature.
3
Analyze the relativity argument
If the earth is a sphere, 'above' is not absolute. What is above for us is below for someone on the opposite side. If God were above, He would be both above and below, which is contradictory.
This shows that 'direction' is relative; God cannot be contained by relative concepts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة السادسة : العالم كرة، وإذا كان كذلك وجب أن لا يكون في الجهة أصلاً، إنما قلنا : إن العالم كرة، وذلك لأنا إذا رصدنا كسوفًا قمريًا فإذا وجدناه في البلاد الشرقية في أول الليل وجداه في البلاد الغربية في آخر الليل، فعلمنا أن أول الليل في المشرق هو آخر الليل بعينه في المغرب، وذلك يدل على أن العالم كرة. إذا ثبت هذا فنقول : الجهة التي فوق رأسنا هي بعينها أسفل لأولئك الذين يكونون على ذلك الوجه الآخر من الأرض، فلو كان تعالى فوقا لنا لكان أسفل بالنسبة إلى سكان ذلك الجانب الآخر من الأرض، ولو كان فوقا لهم لكان أسفل بالنسبة إلينا، فثبت أنه لو كان في جهة لوجب إن يكون أسفل بالنسبة إلى بعض الجوانب، ولما كان ذلك باطلا ثبت أنه تعالى يمتنع كونه تعالى في المكان والجهة.
The sixth proof: the world is a sphere (كرة), and if so, it necessarily follows that He is not in a direction (جهة) at all. We say that the world is a sphere, because when we observe a lunar eclipse (كسوف قمري) and find it in eastern lands at the beginning of the night, we find it in western lands at the end of the night, so we know that the beginning of the night in the east is exactly the end of the night in the west, and that indicates that the world is a sphere. If this is established, we say: the direction that is above our heads is exactly below (أسفل) for those who are on that other side of the earth. So if He were above (فوق) us, He would be below relative to the inhabitants of that other side of the earth, and if He were above them, He would be below relative to us. So it is established that if He were in a direction, He would necessarily be below relative to some sides, and since that is false, it is established that He, exalted, cannot be in place (مكان) and direction.
Source pages p. 113

Commentary
This passage presents the sixth proof against God being in a place or direction. Razi first establishes that the earth is spherical by citing an empirical observation: a lunar eclipse observed in the east at the beginning of the night is seen in the west at the end of the night, proving that the world is a sphere. From this, he argues that a single direction like 'above' is relative: what is above for us is below for people on the opposite side of the earth. Therefore, if God were in a fixed direction, He would be both above and below relative to different observers, which is contradictory. Since this is impossible, God cannot be in any place or direction.

Key Terms
كرة
كسوف قمري
فوق
أسفل
جهة
مكان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The argument only relies on empirical astronomy and has no theological force.
Correction: The empirical proof of the spherical earth is only a premise; the core argument is logical: if the earth is spherical, direction is relative, so God cannot be in an absolute direction.

Checkpoint
How does Razi prove the world is a sphere?
A) By observing lunar eclipses at different longitudes.
B) By rational deduction alone.
C) By citing scripture.
D) By the relativity of above and below.

Key Takeaway
Razi's sixth proof shows that the spherical nature of the earth makes the concept of an absolute direction impossible, thus Allah is beyond place and direction.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you stand to pray and say 'Allahu Akbar', you raise your hands. If Allah is not in any direction, does your heart truly feel that He is closer to you than your jugular vein, or do you still imagine Him 'up there'? What can you do to align your inward state with this truth?
?
This proof shows that 'above' is relative. Yet we read in the Qur'an that Allah is 'above His Throne' (e.g., Surah Taha, 20:5). How do you reconcile this verse with Razi's conclusion? Does your understanding of 'istiwa' change now? Commit to studying the interpretations of the Salaf on this matter.

If you were to explain to a skeptic that Allah is beyond place and direction, would your own life reflect that belief? Where do you seek comfort—in a direction or in the One who is free from direction? What practical changes can you make to live with greater awareness of His transcendence?

The Sixth Proof: The Spherical World Precludes Direction
Razi proves the world is spherical and uses it to deny direction to Allah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Razi's argument that the spherical shape of the world disproves the notion that Allah is in any physical direction.

Core Idea
A spherical world makes 'above' and 'below' relative; Allah cannot be relative.

Razi's sixth proof is a striking blend of empirical observation and rational theology. He first shows that the world is spherical using a lunar eclipse argument, then draws a powerful conclusion: if the world is a sphere, then any direction (like 'above') is relative to where you stand. This leads to a contradiction if Allah were said to be in a direction, proving that Allah transcends all spatial orientation.

Guided Path
1
Observe the lunar eclipse evidence
Read how Razi uses the timing of lunar eclipses in different regions to prove the earth is spherical. Understand why this shows the world is a sphere.
This is a rare use of empirical science in a theological proof.
2
Understand the relativity of direction
Once the world is a sphere, the direction 'above' in one place is 'below' in another. Grasp this key insight.
Imagine two people on opposite sides of the earth.
3
Apply the argument to Allah
If Allah were in a direction, He would be both 'above' and 'below' relative to different observers, which is impossible. Therefore, Allah cannot be in any direction.
This is a reductio ad absurdum argument.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
Razi concludes that Allah is impossible to be in place or direction. Consider how this supports the doctrine of divine transcendence (tanzih).
This is a key affirmation of Allah's incomparability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة السادسة : العالم كرة، وإذا كان كذلك وجب أن لا يكون في الجهة أصلاً، إنما قلنا : إن العالم كرة، وذلك لأنا إذا رصدنا كسوفًا قمريًا فإذا وجدناه في البلاد الشرقية في أول الليل وجداه في البلاد الغربية في آخر الليل، فعلمنا أن أول الليل في المشرق هو آخر الليل بعينه في المغرب، وذلك يدل على أن العالم كرة. إذا ثبت هذا فنقول : الجهة التي فوق رأسنا هي بعينها أسفل لأولئك الذين يكونون على ذلك الوجه الآخر من الأرض، فلو كان تعالى فوقا لنا لكان أسفل بالنسبة إلى سكان ذلك الجانب الآخر من الأرض، ولو كان فوقا لهم لكان أسفل بالنسبة إلينا، فثبت أنه لو كان في جهة لوجب إن يكون أسفل بالنسبة إلى بعض الجوانب، ولما كان ذلك باطلا ثبت أنه تعالى يمتنع كونه تعالى في المكان والجهة.
The sixth proof: The world is a sphere, and if so, then it is necessary that He (exalted) is not in a direction at all. We only say that the world is a sphere because when we observe a lunar eclipse, if we find it in eastern lands at the beginning of the night, we find it in western lands at the end of the night. Thus we know that the beginning of the night in the east is the very end of the night in the west, and that indicates that the world is a sphere. If this is established, then we say: The direction that is above our heads is exactly below for those who are on that other side of the earth. So if He (exalted) were above us, He would be below relative to the inhabitants of that other side of the earth; and if He were above them, He would be below relative to us. Thus it is established that if He were in a direction, He would necessarily be below relative to some sides. And since that is false, it is established that He (exalted) is impossible to be in place and direction.
Source pages p. 113

Commentary
This passage presents the sixth proof (al-ḥujja al-sādisa) that Allah cannot be in a direction (jiha). Razi first establishes that the world is a sphere, using the observation of lunar eclipses: when observed in eastern lands at the beginning of the night and in western lands at the end of the night, it is the same eclipse, proving the earth's curvature. Then he argues that on a sphere, the direction above one point is below another. Therefore, if Allah were above us, He would be below those on the opposite side. This contradiction shows that Allah cannot be in any direction, as it would require Him to be both above and below relative to different observers, which is impossible.

Key Terms
جهة
كرة
كسوف قمري

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Allah is physically above the world, like a king above his throne.
Correction: The spherical nature of the world shows that 'above' is relative; thus Allah cannot be literally above, as that would entail He is also below, which is impossible.

Checkpoint
What observation does Razi use to prove the world is a sphere?
A) The movement of the sun across the sky
B) Lunar eclipses observed at different times in different regions
C) The changing phases of the moon
D) The rotation of the stars around the North Pole

Key Takeaway
The spherical shape of the world shows that Allah cannot be in any direction, as it would lead to a logical contradiction.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

Opponent's Scriptural Evidence for Direction
Razi lists three opponent verses that appear to affirm direction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will identify the three Quranic verses that opponents use to claim Allah is in a direction.

Core Idea
Three verses that seem to point 'above' but are not literal.

Before we examine the rational refutation of direction for Allah, we must first understand what the opponent brings. They rely on apparent meanings of certain verses. Here, Razi lists three key verses that appear to imply that Allah is 'above' or has a direction. Recognizing these verses is the first step.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text once without translating. Notice the words 'استوى' and 'فوق'.
These are the key terms that suggest direction.
2
Read the translation
Now read the literal translation. See how each verse is introduced as giving an 'impression' of direction.
3
Identify each verse and its directional word
List the three verses and note the word that implies direction (e.g., 'على', 'فوق'). Reflect on why these verses might be problematic for divine transcendence.
This prepares you for the refutation in the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما النقل : فهو الألفاظ الموهمة لإثبات الجهة كقوله تعالى : الرَّحْمَنُ عَلَى الْعَرْشِ اسْتَوَى [طه: ٥] وقوله تعالى: ﴿وَهُوَ الْقَاهِرُ فَوْقَ عِبَادِهِ ﴾ [الأنعام: ٦١] ﴾ وقوله تعالى : يَخَافُونَ رَبَّهُم من فوقهم [النحل : ٥٠] .
As for transmitted text: it is the expressions that give the impression of establishing direction, such as His statement, 'The Most Merciful established above the Throne' [Ṭā Hā 5], and His statement, 'And He is the Subduer above His servants' [al-Anʿām 61], and His statement, 'They fear their Lord above them' [al-Naḥl 50].
Source pages p. 113

Commentary
This passage presents the transmitted (naqlī) evidence that the opponent brings to support direction for Allah. They cite three verses: "The Most Merciful established above the Throne" (Ṭā Hā 5), "He is the Subduer above His servants" (al-Anʿām 61), and "They fear their Lord above them" (al-Naḥl 50). These verses use spatial language that can be misinterpreted to mean that Allah is literally in a direction. The term "above" (fawq) is particularly emphasized. Razi will later refute these interpretations.

Refutation of the First Doubt: The Division of Existents
Razi refutes a false dichotomy about existents.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Razi refutes the claim that existents are limited to only two relations (interpenetration or separation by direction) by exposing the logical fallacy of circular reasoning.

Core Idea
A false dichotomy collapses when a third possibility remains open.

In this passage, Imam Razi responds to the first doubt raised by opponents who attempt to limit the possible relations between any two existents to only two categories: interpenetration or separation by direction. He reveals the logical flaw in their reasoning by showing that their argument either assumes the very point in question without proof or falls into circularity, thus rendering it invalid.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its translation once to get a sense of Razi's argument. Notice the concise style and logical structure.
2
Identify the three categories of existents
Razi states that the rational division of existents yields three categories: (1) one interpenetrating the other, (2) separated by direction, (3) neither interpenetrating nor separated. Locate these in the text.
The third category is the key to the refutation.
3
Understand the opponent's claim and Razi's two-pronged response
The opponent claims the third category is impossible. Razi first challenges the claim that this impossibility is known necessarily (by intuition). Then he argues that if it is known by proof, their proof is circular because it assumes the third category is impossible to prove that every two existents must be either interpenetrating or separated.
4
Recognize the logical fallacy: dawr (circularity)
Razi's point is that the opponent's argument commits the fallacy of circular reasoning. Reflect on why this makes their argument invalid.
This is a crucial concept in Islamic logic and kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والجواب عن الشبهة الأولى: لا شك أن قسمة العقل تقتضي انقسام الموجودات إلى ثلاثة أقسام ؛ وذلك لأن كل موجودين فإما أن يكون أحدهما ساريًا في الآخر أو مباينا عنه بالحيز والجهة، أو لا ساريًا فيه ولا مباينا عنه بالحيز، فإن ادعيتم أن القسم الثالث ممتنع الوجود - والعلم بامتناعه ضروري - فقد أبطلناه، وإن سلمتم أن إيطال هذا القسم الثالث ليس معلومًا بالضرورة، بل بالدليل فنقول : قولكم : إن كل موجودين لإما أن يكون أحدهما ساريًا في الآخر أو مباينا عنه بالجهة، إنما يصح عليه لو ثبت فساد القسم الثالث، فإنكم إذا أثبتم فساد القسم الثالث بهذه المقدمة وقع الدور، فيكون ساقطا.
And the answer to the first doubt: There is no doubt that the rational division necessitates the division of existents into three categories. That is because every two existents are either one interpenetrating the other or separated from it by space and direction, or neither interpenetrating it nor separated from it by space. If you claim that the third category is impossible in existence—and knowledge of its impossibility is necessary—then we have refuted that. And if you grant that the invalidation of this third category is not known by necessity, but by proof, then we say: Your statement that every two existents are either one interpenetrating the other or separated from it by direction is only valid if the corruption of the third category is established. For if you establish the corruption of the third category by this premise, circularity occurs, so it falls.
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This passage gives the response (jawāb) to the first doubt (shubha). The opponent claimed that the rational division of existents into three categories: (1) one interpenetrating the other, (2) separated by direction, (3) neither interpenetrating nor separated—and that the third is impossible. Razi points out that if they claim the impossibility is known necessarily (ḍarūra), then he rejects that claim. If they say it is known by proof, then their proof that "every two existents are either interpenetrating or separated" only holds if the third category is already proven impossible, which would be circular (dawr). Thus their argument is invalid.

Key Terms
شبهة
تقسيم
دور
ساري
مباين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some assume that every pair of existents must be either spatially interpenetrating or separated by direction, with no other possibility.
Correction: Razi shows that a third category—neither interpenetrating nor separated—is logically possible, and that the opponent's attempt to rule it out is either baseless or circular.

Checkpoint
What logical fallacy does Razi accuse the opponent of in the first doubt?
A) Begging the question
B) Circular reasoning (dawr)
C) Infinite regress
D) False dichotomy

Key Takeaway
Imam Razi refutes the doubt by affirming a threefold division of existents and exposing the opponent's circular reasoning, thereby defending the possibility of a relation beyond interpenetration and spatial separation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are you ever too quick to accept a binary choice about God's nature (e.g., He is either distant or interwoven) because it feels simpler than considering a third, transcendent possibility? What might you need to release to remain open to the truth?
?
When you defend your beliefs, do you ever catch yourself using reasoning that assumes what you're trying to prove? How honest are you willing to be about the weaknesses in your own arguments?
?
Razi defends a third category that is neither interpenetration nor separation. In your relationship with God, do you allow for a connection that is neither worldly attachment nor abstract detachment? What would change if you did?

Refutation of the Second Doubt: Essence vs. Attribute
Razi argues that a body's specification to direction may be due to its specific essence, not a shared property.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Razi's argument that a body's specification to direction is due to its essence, not a separate attribute, thereby refuting the analogy between Allah and bodies.

Core Idea
A body's direction is essential, not attributable; the analogy to Allah fails.

Razi continues his refutation of doubts about divine transcendence. The second doubt argues that since Allah is self-subsistent like bodies, He must also occupy direction. Razi responds by questioning the premise: perhaps a body's direction is inherent to its essence, not a separate attribute. This passage presents that argument using an infinite regress to show that specification cannot be endlessly attributed.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice how Razi presents his answer as a rhetorical question.
This is a refutation of a doubt.
2
Identify the doubt
What is the second doubt? It claims that since Allah is self-subsistent like bodies, He must occupy direction. Find where Razi addresses this.
The doubt is not explicitly stated here but implied.
3
Understand the infinite regress
Razi argues that if specification to direction were due to an attribute, that attribute would itself need an attribute, leading to infinite regress. This forces the conclusion that direction is essential to body.
This is a classic kalam argument.
4
Apply the conclusion
Since direction is essential to body, it does not apply to other self-subsistent beings like Allah. Therefore, the analogy fails.
This protects divine transcendence.
5
Reflect on the methodology
Note how Razi uses logical reasoning (infinite regress) to defend theological doctrines. This is a hallmark of kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الجواب عن الشبهة الثانية فنقول : لم لا يجوز أن يكون كون الجسم مختصا بالحيز والجهة بذاته المخصوصة لا لوصف آخر ؟ وذلك لأن اختصاص الذات بالصفة لو كان لأجل صفة أخرى، لزم التسلسل، فلا بد من الانتهاء إلى ما كان ثابتا له لذاته فلم لا يجوز أن يكون كون الجسم مختصا بالحيز والجهة من هذا الباب؟
And as for the answer to the second doubt, we say: Why is it not permissible that a body's being specified to space and direction is due to its specific essence, not due to another attribute? That is because if the specification of an essence to an attribute were due to another attribute, infinite regress would follow. So it is necessary to end at what is established for it by its essence. So why is it not permissible that a body's being specified to space and direction is of this kind?
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This passage answers the second doubt, which likened Allah to a body in being self-subsistent and therefore occupying direction. Razi responds by asking why it is not possible that a body's being specified to a direction is due to its specific essence (dhāt), not a separate attribute. He argues that if specification were due to an attribute, that attribute would require another attribute, leading to infinite regress (tasalsul). Therefore, it is reasonable that direction is essential to body, but not to every self-subsistent being. Thus the analogy fails.

Key Terms
ذات
صفة
تسلسل
اختصاص

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If two things share a property (self-subsistence), they must share all properties (direction).
Correction: Razi shows that direction may be essential to body and thus not transferable to Allah.

Checkpoint
What argument does Razi use against the second doubt?
A) That direction is a property of bodies only
B) That infinite regress would result if direction were due to an attribute
C) That Allah's essence is unknowable
D) That bodies are not self-subsistent

Key Takeaway
Razi refutes the analogy by arguing that a body's direction is essential to it, not a necessary attribute of all self-subsistent beings.

?

Refutation of the Claim that the Direction Above is Noblest
Razi enumerates four rational refutations of the third doubt.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Razi refutes the claim that Allah must be above because that direction is noblest, using four rational arguments.

Core Idea
Rhetorical honor does not prove direction for Allah.

The third doubt claims that the direction 'above' is the noblest, so Allah must be there. Imam al-Razi dismantles this with four crisp rational arguments, showing that the premise is rhetorical, the world's sphericity destroys absolute 'above', and any attempt to define Allah's location leads to absurdity. Let's study his refutation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four flaws
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice that Razi introduces four points (وجوه) to refute the doubt. Try to list them as you read.
2
First flaw: rhetorical premise
Understand that the opponent's statement is a rhetorical (خطابية) premise, which cannot be used in rational (عقليات) discussions. This dismisses the argument at its root.
3
Second flaw: spherical world
Grasp that because the world is a sphere, any direction considered 'above' for one point is 'below' for another. There is no absolute 'above' in the universe.
4
Third flaw: infinite or finite extension
Analyze the dilemma: if Allah's essence extends infinitely upward, no point is absolutely above; if it has a limit, then above that limit is void, making the void higher. Either way, Allah cannot be absolutely above.
5
Fourth flaw: honor belongs to place not occupant
Reflect on the argument that honor from direction belongs primarily to the place, only accidentally to the occupant. If Allah occupied a noble direction, the direction would be nobler than Him—an absurdity.
The text cuts off before completing this point, but the logic is clear.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والجواب عن الشبهة الثالثة : وهي قولهم : أشرف الجهات جهة العلو. فنقول : هذا الكلام ساقط من وجوه : الأول : أن هذا الكلام مقدمة خطابية فلا يلتفت إليها في العقليات. الثاني : أنا قد بينا أنه لما كان العالم كرة كان كل جهة يشار إليها فهي وإن كانت فوق بالنسبة إلى البعض لكنها تحت بالنسبة إلى الباقين. والثالث : أنه إما أن يقال لا نهاية لامتداد ذات الله من جهة العلو أو يكون لامتداد ذاته نهاية فإن كان الأول لم يفرض في ذاته نقطة إلا وفوقها نقطة أخرى، ولا شيء يفرض فيه إلا وهو سفل لا علو مطلق وإن كان الثاني افترض فوق طرفه العلوي خلاء، فكان ذلك الخلاء أعلى منه، ولم يكن علوّا مطلقا. والرابع : أن الشرف الحاصل بسبب العلو بالجهة يكون حاصلا للحيز والجهة بالذات، ويكون حاصلا للمتمكن بالعرض، بسبب أنه حصل في ذلك المكان، فحصول هذا الشرف للمكان ،والجهة أتم مما للمتمكن، فلو كان الباري تعالى
And the answer to the third doubt, which is their statement: The noblest of directions is the direction of height. We say: This statement is invalid on several counts. First: This statement is a rhetorical premise, so it is not to be considered in rational matters. Second: We have already shown that since the world is a sphere, every direction that is pointed to, even if it is above relative to some, is below relative to others. Third: It is either said that there is no end to the extension of Allah's essence from the direction of height, or that His essence's extension has an end. If the first, no point is assumed in His essence except that there is another point above it, and nothing is assumed in it except that it is lower, with no absolute height. If the second, then above its upper extremity there is void, so that void is higher than it, and it is not absolute height. Fourth: The honor obtained due to height in direction accrues to the space and direction essentially, and accrues to the occupant accidentally, due to his being in that place. So the attainment of this honor for the place and direction is more complete than for the occupant. So if the Creator (exalted) were…
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This passage presents Razi's refutation of the third doubt, that the noblest direction is above. He gives four points (wujūh). First, the opponent's statement is a rhetorical (khiṭābī) premise, not to be relied upon in rational matters. Second, since the world is spherical, any direction that is above for some is below for others, so there is no absolute above. Third, if Allah's essence has no limit from above, then no point can be said to be absolutely above; if it does have a limit, then above that limit would be void, making Him not absolutely above. Fourth, the honor (sharaf) gained from direction belongs primarily to the direction itself, and only secondarily to the being located there; so the argument would require Allah to be in a direction that is nobler than He, which is absurd. The text cuts off at 'فلو كان الباري تعالى' but the argument is clear: it would be impossible.

Key Terms
خطابية
عقليات
خلاء
علو مطلق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The direction above is inherently nobler than other directions, so Allah must be located there.
Correction: This is a rhetorical premise, not a rational one. Moreover, the sphericity of the world makes 'above' relative, and any attempt to assign Allah a direction leads to absurdities (infinite/ finite extension, honor belonging to place).

Checkpoint
How many points does Razi give in refuting the third doubt?
A) Two
B) Three
C) Four
D) Five

Key Takeaway
Allah is beyond direction and place; arguments based on honor are rhetorical, not rational, and lead to absurdities.

Razi dismisses rhetorical arguments as invalid in rational theology. In your own faith, do you rely more on 'nice-sounding' ideas about Allah or on sound knowledge? What is one teaching from this lesson that you will study further to deepen your understanding?

Definition of Transmitted Proofs (al-Naql)
Razi defines transmitted proofs and gives examples from the Quran.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand what transmitted proofs (al-naql) are according to Imam Razi and why they are problematic when interpreted literally.

Core Idea
Transmitted proofs are expressions that seem to imply direction but must be interpreted metaphorically.

Imam Razi begins his discussion of transmitted proofs by defining them as ambiguous expressions from revelation that give the false impression of God being in a direction. He cites several Quranic verses that are often misunderstood. In this lesson, we will examine his definition and the verses he uses to illustrate the issue.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition
Read the Arabic definition of al-naql and its translation. Note that it describes transmitted proofs as 'expressions that give the false impression of affirming direction'.
2
Examine the Quranic examples
Look at the three verses Razi cites. Why might these verses be misinterpreted as implying direction?
These verses are often used by anthropomorphists to claim God has a body or location.
3
Understand the significance
Reflect on why Razi starts with this definition. It sets up the need to answer objections that these verses contradict divine transcendence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما النقل : فهو الألفاظ الموهمة لإثبات الجهة كقوله تعالى : الرَّحْمَنُ عَلَى الْعَرْشِ اسْتَوَى [طه: ٥] وقوله تعالى: ﴿وَهُوَ الْقَاهِرُ فَوْقَ عِبَادِهِ ﴾ [الأنعام: ٦١] ﴾ وقوله تعالى : يَخَافُونَ رَبَّهُم من فوقهم [النحل : ٥٠] . والجواب عن الشبهة الأولى: لا شك أن قسمة العقل تقتضي انقسام الموجودات إلى ثلاثة أقسام ؛ وذلك لأن كل موجودين فإما أن يكون أحدهما ساريًا في الآخر أو مباينا عنه بالحيز والجهة، أو لا ساريًا فيه ولا مباينا عنه بالحيز، فإن ادعيتم أن القسم الثالث ممتنع الوجود - والعلم بامتناعه ضروري - فقد أبطلناه، وإن سلمتم أن إبطال هذا القسم الثالث ليس معلومًا بالضرورة، بل بالدليل فنقول : قولكم : إن كل موجودين إما أن يكون أحدهما ساريًا في الآخر أو مباينا عنه بالجهة، إنما يصح عليه لو ثبت فساد القسم الثالث، فإنكم إذا أثبتم فساد القسم الثالث بهذه المقدمة وقع الدور، فيكون ساقطا.
As for transmitted proof: it is the expressions that give the false impression of affirming direction, like His saying, the Most High: 'The Most Merciful established Himself above the Throne' [Ta-Ha: 5], and His saying: 'And He is the Subjugator over His servants' [Al-An'am: 61], and His saying: 'They fear their Lord above them' [An-Nahl: 50]. And the answer to the first objection: There is no doubt that rational division necessitates the division of existents into three categories; that is because any two existents are either such that one permeates the other, or they are separate from each other by location and direction, or neither permeating nor separate by location. If you claim that the third category is impossible—and knowledge of its impossibility is necessary—then we have refuted that. And if you concede that nullifying this third category is not known by necessity but by proof, then we say: Your statement that 'any two existents are either that one permeates the other or separate by direction' is only valid if the corruption of the third category is established; for if you establish the corruption of the third category by this premise, a circularity occurs, so it is invalid.
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This passage begins by defining transmitted proofs (al-naql) as ambiguous expressions that suggest direction, citing Quranic verses. It then addresses the first objection (al-shubha al-ūlā). The objection likely argued that all existents must be either permeating through another or spatially separate, so God must be in a direction. Razi counters by first stating a rational division of existents into three categories: (1) one permeating another, (2) separate by location/direction, (3) neither permeating nor separate. He then poses a dilemma to the objector: if they claim the third category is impossible by necessity, that claim is false; if they admit it requires proof, then their own premise—that all existents are either permeating or separate—depends on proving the impossibility of the third category, leading to circular reasoning. Thus the objection collapses.

Key Terms
النقل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that Quranic verses about God being 'above' or 'on the Throne' must be taken literally, implying a physical location for God.
Correction: Imam Razi clarifies that these verses are classified as 'transmitted proofs' that give a false impression (muwahhima) of direction; they require metaphorical interpretation to uphold God's transcendence.

Checkpoint
According to Razi, what are transmitted proofs (al-naql)?
A) Verses that prove God's existence
B) Expressions that give the false impression of affirming direction
C) Verses about the afterlife
D) Rational arguments for God's attributes

Key Takeaway
Transmitted proofs are Quranic expressions that seem to imply direction but must be interpreted non-literally to maintain divine transcendence.

6 min
The First Objection: Division of Existents
Razi answers the first objection by dividing existents into three categories and exposing circular reasoning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Razi refutes the first objection that all existents must be either permeating or separate, using a threefold division of existents and exposing circular reasoning.

Core Idea
Razi divides existents into three categories, not two, breaking the objector's premise and exposing a logical circle.

The first objection against divine transcendence claims that all existents are either permeating through another or spatially separate, leaving no room for a none-of-the-above category. Razi counters by introducing a rational division of existents into three categories and then catching the objector in a circular argument. This lesson unpacks that argument.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
Read the beginning of the answer. The objection is that any two existents must be either one permeating the other (sārin) or separate by location (mubāyin). Razi will challenge this dichotomy.
2
Learn the threefold division
Razi introduces a third category: neither permeating nor separate. Find it in the text. Why is this third category necessary?
This third category is crucial for God's existence, as He is neither inside nor spatially separate from creation.
3
Follow the circularity argument
Razi then presents a dilemma: if the objector claims the third category is impossible by necessity, that claim is false; if they admit it requires proof, their own argument becomes circular. Trace this reasoning.
4
Reflect on the significance
Consider why this argument is important for defending God's transcendence. It refutes the idea that God must be in a direction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما النقل : فهو الألفاظ الموهمة لإثبات الجهة كقوله تعالى : الرَّحْمَنُ عَلَى الْعَرْشِ اسْتَوَى [طه: ٥] وقوله تعالى: ﴿وَهُوَ الْقَاهِرُ فَوْقَ عِبَادِهِ ﴾ [الأنعام: ٦١] ﴾ وقوله تعالى : يَخَافُونَ رَبَّهُم من فوقهم [النحل : ٥٠] . والجواب عن الشبهة الأولى: لا شك أن قسمة العقل تقتضي انقسام الموجودات إلى ثلاثة أقسام ؛ وذلك لأن كل موجودين فإما أن يكون أحدهما ساريًا في الآخر أو مباينا عنه بالحيز والجهة، أو لا ساريًا فيه ولا مباينا عنه بالحيز، فإن ادعيتم أن القسم الثالث ممتنع الوجود - والعلم بامتناعه ضروري - فقد أبطلناه، وإن سلمتم أن إبطال هذا القسم الثالث ليس معلومًا بالضرورة، بل بالدليل فنقول : قولكم : إن كل موجودين إما أن يكون أحدهما ساريًا في الآخر أو مباينا عنه بالجهة، إنما يصح عليه لو ثبت فساد القسم الثالث، فإنكم إذا أثبتم فساد القسم الثالث بهذه المقدمة وقع الدور، فيكون ساقطا.
As for transmitted proof: it is the expressions that give the false impression of affirming direction, like His saying, the Most High: 'The Most Merciful established Himself above the Throne' [Ta-Ha: 5], and His saying: 'And He is the Subjugator over His servants' [Al-An'am: 61], and His saying: 'They fear their Lord above them' [An-Nahl: 50]. And the answer to the first objection: There is no doubt that rational division necessitates the division of existents into three categories; that is because any two existents are either such that one permeates the other, or they are separate from each other by location and direction, or neither permeating nor separate by location. If you claim that the third category is impossible—and knowledge of its impossibility is necessary—then we have refuted that. And if you concede that nullifying this third category is not known by necessity but by proof, then we say: Your statement that 'any two existents are either that one permeates the other or separate by direction' is only valid if the corruption of the third category is established; for if you establish the corruption of the third category by this premise, a circularity occurs, so it is invalid.
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This passage begins by defining transmitted proofs (al-naql) as ambiguous expressions that suggest direction, citing Quranic verses. It then addresses the first objection (al-shubha al-ūlā). The objection likely argued that all existents must be either permeating through another or spatially separate, so God must be in a direction. Razi counters by first stating a rational division of existents into three categories: (1) one permeating another, (2) separate by location/direction, (3) neither permeating nor separate. He then poses a dilemma to the objector: if they claim the third category is impossible by necessity, that claim is false; if they admit it requires proof, then their own premise—that all existents are either permeating or separate—depends on proving the impossibility of the third category, leading to circular reasoning. Thus the objection collapses.

Key Terms
الشبهة
قسمة العقل
الساري
المباين
الدور

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that all existents must be either inside another thing or spatially separate, leaving no possibility for a transcendent God.
Correction: Razi shows that a third category is rationally necessary: existents that are neither permeating nor separate, which applies to God.

Checkpoint
What is the third category in Razi's division of existents?
A) Impossible
B) Neither permeating nor separate by location
C) Both permeating and separate
D) None of the above

Key Takeaway
Razi refutes the first objection by introducing a third rational category of existents and exposing circular reasoning in the objector's argument.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
Razi reveals that the objector's premise already assumes the conclusion. Is there any area of your faith where your reasoning is subtly circular—where you assume what you are trying to prove? Ask Allah for sincerity and clarity, and be willing to abandon flawed reasoning no matter how comfortable it feels.

Razi's Answer: Location as an Essential Property
Razi refutes the claim that location requires a separate attribute, using the infinite regress argument.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Razi's argument that a body's location can be essential (by its own essence) rather than requiring a separate attribute, and how this avoids the problem of infinite regress.

Core Idea
Some properties are essential, stopping the infinite chain of attributes.

This passage presents Razi's response to an objection: if everything in a location has an attribute of location, then God—if He were in a location—would need such an attribute, implying composition. Razi counters by questioning why location cannot be an essential property of a body itself, without a separate attribute. His reasoning uses the principle that chains of attributes must end at something essential, otherwise infinite regress occurs. Understanding this argument helps clarify how kalam theologians differentiate between essential and accidental properties.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
First, read the Arabic passage slowly, then the English translation. Notice the rhetorical question at the start: 'Why is it not permissible...' This sets up the rebuttal.
The key term 'tasalsul' (infinite regress) appears here.
2
Identify the objection being answered
Although the objection is not quoted directly, the passage is a response. Based on the context, the objection claimed that a body's presence in a location is due to an attribute. Razi challenges this assumption.
Razi's strategy is to question the necessity of an attribute for location.
3
Follow the infinite regress argument
Razi argues that if every property required another property to explain it, we would have an infinite regress. Therefore, there must be properties that belong to the essence itself. Location could be one such property.
This is a foundational argument in kalam for establishing essential attributes.
4
Apply the conclusion to the case of location
Razi concludes that location may be essential to a body, thus not requiring an additional attribute. This weakens the objection against God (since God is not a body, but the point is about the principle).
The argument is about bodies; the application to God would be by analogy or distinction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الجواب عن الشبهة الثانية فنقول : لم لا يجوز أن يكون كون الجسم مختصا بالحيز والجهة بذاته المخصوصة لا لوصف آخر ؟ وذلك لأن اختصاص الذات بالصفة لو كان لأجل صفة أخرى، لزم التسلسل، فلا بد من الانتهاء إلى ما كان ثابتا له لذاته فلم لا يجوز أن يكون كون الجسم مختصا بالحيز والجهة من هذا الباب؟
As for the answer to the second objection, we say: Why is it not permissible that a body's being specific to a location and direction is due to its own particular essence, not due to another attribute? That is because if the specificity of the essence by an attribute were due to another attribute, an infinite regress would follow, so it must terminate at that which is established for it by its essence. So why is it not permissible that a body's being specific to location and direction is of this kind?
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This passage answers the second objection, which likely argued that God must have an attribute (like being in a direction) because everything that exists in a place does so through an attribute. Razi responds by questioning why a body cannot be specific to a location by its very essence, without requiring a separate attribute. He argues that if every attribute required another attribute to explain its connection to the essence, an infinite regress (tasalsul) would result. Therefore, the chain must end with something that is true of the essence by itself. Hence, location and direction could be essential properties of a body, not necessarily requiring a separate attribute. This undermines the objection that God must have an attribute of location.

Key Terms
الحيز
الجهة
الذات
الصفة
التسلسل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Every property of a body (like its location) must be due to a separate attribute.
Correction: Razi argues that some properties can be essential (by the essence itself), and this is necessary to avoid infinite regress.

Checkpoint

B) Infinite regress
C) Circularity

Key Takeaway
Razi uses the impossibility of infinite regress to argue that some properties, like location, can be essential to a body, thus not requiring a separate attribute.

Razi's Four Arguments Against Divine Location
Razi enumerates four arguments refuting the honor of direction 'above'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the argument that 'above' is the most honorable direction fails in rational theology, and how Razi dismantles it with four distinct objections.

Core Idea
Honor through location is relative; the Creator cannot be bound by direction.

This lesson deals with Razi's response to those who argue that because the direction of 'above' is most honorable, God must be above. Razi provides four incisive arguments showing why this premise is invalid in rational discourse. We will examine each argument in turn and see how they collectively safeguard divine transcendence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Carefully read the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Note the four distinct points Razi enumerates.
The passage uses 'الوجوه' to introduce each argument.
2
Distinguish rhetorical from rational
Identify Razi's first argument: the premise about honor is rhetorical, not intellectually rigorous. Understand why such premises are rejected in kalam.
Rhetorical arguments may persuade the masses but have no place in rational theology.
3
Apply the spherical world argument
Reflect on the second argument: the earth is a sphere, so 'above' is relative. What is above for one is below for another, destroying any absolute direction.
This argument uses cosmology familiar to the audience.
4
Analyze the dilemma about God's essence
Consider the third argument: if God's extension in the above direction is infinite, every point has another above it; if finite, empty space above would be higher. Neither yields an absolute highest point.
This shows the absurdity of assigning a directional limit to God.
5
Grasp the honor transfer absurdity
Understand the fourth argument: honor from location belongs essentially to the place, not the occupant. If God were in a direction, the place would be more honored—an impossible conclusion.
This final argument seals the refutation by showing the logical consequence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والجواب عن الشبهة الثالثة : وهي قولهم : أشرف الجهات جهة العلو. فنقول : هذا الكلام ساقط من وجوه : الأول : أن هذا الكلام مقدمة خطابية فلا يلتفت إليها في العقليات. الثاني : أنا قد بينا أنه لما كان العالم كرة كان كل جهة يشار إليها فهي وإن كانت فوق بالنسبة إلى البعض لكنها تحت بالنسبة إلى الباقين. والثالث : أنه إما أن يقال لا نهاية لامتداد ذات الله من جهة العلو أو يكون لامتداد ذاته نهاية فإن كان الأول لم يفرض في ذاته نقطة إلا وفوقها نقطة أخرى، ولا شيء يفرض فيه إلا وهو سفل لا علو مطلق وإن كان الثاني افترض فوق طرفه العلوي خلاء، فكان ذلك الخلاء أعلى منه، ولم يكن علوّا مطلقا. والرابع : أن الشرف الحاصل بسبب العلو بالجهة يكون حاصلا للحيز والجهة بالذات، ويكون حاصلا للمتمكن بالعرض، بسبب أنه حصل في ذلك المكان، فحصول هذا الشرف للمكان والجهة أتم مما للمتمكن، فلو كان الباري تعالى حاصلا في الجهة لزم أن يكون المكان أشرف في هذا الباب من الباري، وهو محال.
And the answer to the third objection—which is their saying: 'The most honorable of directions is the direction of above.' We say: This statement is invalid in several respects: First: This statement is a rhetorical premise, so it is not heeded in intellectual matters. Second: We have shown that since the world is a sphere, every direction that is pointed to is, although it is 'above' relative to some, it is 'below' relative to others. Third: Either it is said that there is no end to the extension of God's essence in the direction of above, or His essence has an end. If the first, then no point is assumed in His essence except that above it is another point, and nothing can be assumed in it except that it is low, not absolute high. If the second, then above its upper extremity emptiness is assumed, so that emptiness would be higher than it, and it would not be absolute high. Fourth: The honor obtained due to being above in direction belongs to the location and direction essentially, and belongs to the occupant accidentally because it occupies that place. So the occurrence of this honor for the location and direction is more complete than that for the occupant. If the Exalted Creator were to occupy a direction, it would necessitate that the location is more honored in this regard than the Creator, which is impossible.
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This passage addresses the third objection, which asserts that the direction 'above' is the most honorable, implying God must be above. Razi dismantles this with four points. First, he dismisses the premise as rhetorical (khiṭābiyya), not valid in rational theology. Second, he invokes the spherical nature of the world: what is 'above' for one is 'below' for another, so there is no absolute above. Third, he examines the implications for God's essence: if His extension in the 'above' direction is infinite, every point has another above it, so no point is absolutely high; if finite, there would be empty space above His extremity, making that emptiness higher—neither yields an absolute highest direction. Fourth, he argues that honor due to being in a high place belongs primarily to the place, not the occupant; if God were in a place, the place would be more honored, which is absurd. Thus the objection fails.

Key Terms
الجهة
العلو
خطابي
كرة
الخلاء
الشرف
المتمكن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The direction 'above' is an absolute and most honorable direction, so God must be above.
Correction: Razi shows that 'above' is relative (due to spherical Earth), and even if absolute, the implications for God's essence lead to absurdities, and honor belongs to place not occupant.

Checkpoint
According to Razi's second argument against the 'above' objection, why is there no absolute direction of 'above'?
A) Because the world is flat
B) Because the world is spherical
C) Because God is everywhere
D) Because directions are imaginary

Key Takeaway
Razi refutes the honor-of-direction argument by showing its rhetorical nature, the relativity of 'above', the logical difficulties for God's essence, and the absurdity of exalting a place over the Creator.

Refuting Spatial Location from Ritual Gestures
Razi refutes the objection from raising hands to heaven by citing prostration on earth.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Razi uses parity of reasoning to refute the claim that raising hands to heaven implies God is in heaven.

Core Idea
Gestures don't locate God—raising hands and prostrating prove nothing about divine location.

Razi addresses an objection that uses the common practice of raising hands during supplication to argue that God must be in the heavens. He responds with a clever counterexample: if that logic were sound, then prostrating with the forehead on the ground would equally prove God is on earth. Since no Muslim accepts that, the original argument collapses.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage and its literal English translation to grasp Razi's concise argument.
Notice the conditional structure: 'if ... then ...'.
2
Identify the objection and counterexample
The objection: raising hands to heaven proves God is in heaven. Razi's counterexample: placing forehead on ground (prostration) would prove God is on earth.
Both actions are acts of worship, so the logic is parallel.
3
Understand the logical parity
Razi uses a reductio ad absurdum: if the premise (gesture implies location) is accepted, it leads to an unacceptable conclusion (God on earth). Therefore the premise must be rejected.
This is a common dialectical method in kalam.
4
Reflect on the refutation's strength
The refutation does not deny that God is in heaven; it denies that ritual gestures can be used as proof for location. It preserves divine transcendence beyond spatial limits.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الجواب عن الشبهة الرابعة : فهو أنه لو كان رفع الأيدي إلى السماء يدل على كون المعبود في السماء لوجب أن يدل وضع الجبهة على الأرض على أنه في الأرض، ولما بطل ذلك فكذا ما قالوا.
As for the answer to the fourth objection: It is that if raising hands to the sky indicates that the object of worship is in the sky, then it would necessarily follow that placing the forehead on the ground indicates that He is on the ground. And since that is invalid, so too is what they said.
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This short passage answers the fourth objection, which apparently uses the practice of raising hands during supplication to argue that God is in the heavens. Razi points out the inconsistency: if raising hands toward heaven proves God is there, then prostrating by putting the forehead on the ground would equally prove God is on the earth. Since the latter is not taken as proof (and is invalid), the former is also invalid. The objection is refuted by a parity of reasoning.

Key Terms
رفع الأيدي
السماء
وضع الجبهة
الأرض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Raising hands in supplication proves God is above in a literal, spatial sense.
Correction: Razi shows that this is not a consistent proof because prostration would then prove God is below, which is not accepted.

Checkpoint

A) Pointing fingers
B) Kneeling in prayer
C) Placing the forehead on the ground
D) Closing eyes during prayer

Key Takeaway
Razi refutes the spatial argument by showing its premise leads to absurdity when applied to prostration.

Razi's Reductio on Raising Hands
Imam Razi refutes the fourth doubt using reductio ad absurdum.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Razi refutes the claim that raising hands indicates God's location by using a reductio ad absurdum argument.

Core Idea
If raising hands implies God is in heaven, then prostrating would imply He is on earth — an absurdity.

Imam Razi addresses the fourth doubt, which attempts to prove divine location from the act of raising hands in supplication. He uses a powerful logical counter: if that reasoning were valid, then the same logic would force us to accept that prostrating (placing the forehead on the ground) means God is on earth. Since that is clearly false, the original argument collapses.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Notice the structure: 'if ... then ... and since that is false, so too is what they said.'
The passage is a single sentence, but it packs a complete logical argument.
2
Identify the opponent's premise
The opponent claims that raising hands to heaven indicates that God is in heaven. Razi takes this premise and applies it to another ritual action: prostrating.
The key is the parallel between raising hands and placing the forehead.
3
Understand the reductio ad absurdum
If the opponent's reasoning were consistent, then prostrating would indicate God is on earth. Since that conclusion is false for Muslims, the original premise must also be false.
This shows that ritual actions do not imply God's spatial location.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الجواب عن الشبهة الرابعة : فهو أنه لو كان رفع الأيدي إلى السماء يدل على كون المعبود في السماء لوجب أن يدل وضع الجبهة على الأرض على أنه في الأرض، ولما بطل ذلك فكذا ما قالوا.
As for the answer to the fourth doubt: it is that if raising hands to heaven indicated that the object of worship is in heaven, then it would be necessary that placing the forehead on the ground indicates that He is in the earth. And since that is false, so too is what they said.
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of a specific doubt (shubha). Imam Razi answers the fourth doubt, which presumably argued that raising hands towards heaven in supplication indicates that God is located in heaven. He counters by showing that the same logic would lead to an absurd conclusion: if raising hands indicates location, then prostrating (placing the forehead on the ground) would indicate that God is on earth. Since this conclusion is false (لما بطل ذلك), the original inference is invalid. The argument is a reductio ad absurdum, demonstrating inconsistency in the opponent's reasoning.

Key Terms
شبهة رابعة
رفع الأيدي
وضع الجبهة
معبود

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Razi is denying that raising hands in supplication has any meaning or significance.
Correction: Razi does not deny the act itself; he denies that it implies God's spatial location. The act remains valid worship, but it does not prove that God resides in heaven.

C) Rejecting the practice of raising hands
D) Appealing to consensus

Key Takeaway
Razi demonstrates that inferring God's location from ritual actions leads to contradictions, preserving divine transcendence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Classification of Christian Views on Indwelling and Union
Razi classifies Christian positions on hulul/ittihad into a precise division.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the categories Imam Razi identifies in Christian doctrines of indwelling and union, and why a precise division is necessary before refutation.

Core Idea
Christian views on God's relation to Jesus are not monolithic; Razi maps them systematically.

Imam Razi begins the ninth issue by acknowledging the confusion in Christian statements about hulul (indwelling) and ittihad (union). To refute them properly, he first establishes a clear classification of all possible positions. This passage presents that classification, which covers whether the indwelling concerns God's essence or attributes, and whether it relates to Jesus' spirit or body, along with alternative views like bestowed power or honorary sonship.

Guided Path
1
Read the classification passage
Read the Arabic passage from the beginning to 'فهذه الوجوه التي يحتملها كلامهم'. Then read the translation. Notice the logical structure: Razi first presents the main branches (hulul vs. ittihad), then sub-branches (essence vs. attribute, spirit vs. body), and finally two alternative views.
The classification is a disjunctive enumeration: either hulul or ittihad; if hulul, then either essence or attribute; if essence/attribute, then either Jesus' spirit or body; otherwise, other views.
2
Identify the six possibilities
List the six possible positions that Imam Razi extracts from Christian discourse. Check your list against the commentary below.
The possibilities are: (1) hulul of essence in Jesus' spirit, (2) hulul of essence in Jesus' body, (3) hulul of attribute in Jesus' spirit, (4) hulul of attribute in Jesus' body, (5) ittihad, (6) bestowed power, (7) honorary sonship. Actually ittihad also has sub-branches but Razi doesn't enumerate them here.
3
Reflect on the purpose of classification
Ask yourself: Why does Imam Razi begin with a classification before refuting? How does this method strengthen his argument?
Classification ensures that no position is left unexamined, and each can be refuted individually.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسألة التاسعة في أنه تعالى يستحيل أن تحل ذاته في شيء ويستحيل أن تحل صفته في شيء اعلم أن النصارى يذكرون الحلول تارة والاتحاد أخرى، وكلامهم في غاية الخبط، ونحن نذكر تقسيما مضبوطًا فنقول : القوم إما أن يقولوا بالحلول أو بالاتحاد، إما لذات الله تعالى أو لصفة من صفاته إما بالنسبة إلى روح عيسى عليه السلام أو بالنسبة إلى بدنه، وإما أن لا يقولوا بشيء من ذلك، بل يقولوا : إنه تعالى أعطاه الله قدرة على خلق الأجسام والحياة، وعلمًا بالمغيبات وإما أن لا يقولوا بذلك أيضًا، بل يقولوا إنه تعالى سماه ابنا على سبيل التشريف كما سمى إبراهيم عليه السلام خليلا على سبيل التشريف فهذه الوجوه التي يحتملها كلامهم. ونقول : أما القول بالحلول فهو باطل لأنه تعالى لو حل في شيء لكان إما أن يحل مع وجوب أن يحل أو جواز أن يحل والأول باطل لوجهين : الأول : أن ذلك يقتضي إما حدوث الحال أو قدم المحل، وكلاهما محالان. والثاني : أنه لما حل مع وجوب أن يحل كانت ذاته مفتقرة إلى ذلك المحل، والمفتقر إلى الغير ممكن بالذات. وأما القسم الثاني وهو أنه تعالى يحل مع جواز أن يحل فهذا أيضًا باطل ؛ لأن المعقول من الحلول كون الحال مفتقرًا إلى المحل ومحتاجا إليه، وإذا لم يوجد هذا المعنى لم يتحقق معنى الحلول. فإن قيل : لم لا يجوز أن يقال: إنه حل مع وجوب أن يحل، قوله : يلزم إما قدم المحل أو حدوث الحال. قلنا لا نسلم ولم لا يجوز أن يقال: إن ذاته يوجب لذاته الحلول في المحل، بشرط وجود ذلك المحل، وقبل وجود المحل لم يكن شرط هذا الاقتضاء
The Ninth Issue: That it is impossible for His essence to indwell in anything and impossible for His attribute to indwell in anything. Know that Christians mention indwelling (hulul) sometimes and union (ittihad) at other times, and their speech is extremely confused. And we mention a precise division and say: The people either say by indwelling or by union; either concerning the essence of God or concerning one of His attributes; either in relation to the spirit of Jesus, peace be upon him, or in relation to his body; or they do not say any of that, but say: He gave him power over creating bodies and life, and knowledge of the unseen; or they do not say that either, but say that He called him a son by way of honor, just as He called Abraham, peace be upon him, a friend (khalil) by way of honor. So these are the possibilities that their speech admits. And we say: As for the statement of indwelling, it is false, because if He indwells in something, then either He indwells with necessity of indwelling or with possibility of indwelling. The first is false for two reasons: First, that necessitates either the temporality of the indweller (al-hall) or the pre-eternity of the locus (al-mahall), and both are impossible. Second, that when He indwells with necessity of indwelling, His essence becomes dependent on that locus, and what is dependent on another is contingent by essence. As for the second division, that He indwells with possibility of indwelling, this is also false, because the intelligible meaning of indwelling is that the indweller is dependent on the locus and in need of it, and if this meaning does not exist, the meaning of indwelling is not realized. If it is said: Why is it not permissible to say that He indwells with necessity of indwelling, and his saying 'it necessitates either the pre-eternity of the locus or the temporality of the indweller'? We say: We do not accept. And why is it not permissible to say that His essence necessitates for itself indwelling in the locus, conditioned upon the existence of that locus, and before the existence of the locus the condition for this necessitation did not exist?
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage is a classification and refutation. Imam Razi begins the ninth issue (al-mas'ala al-tasi'a) on the impossibility of God's essence or attribute indwelling in anything. First, he classifies Christian views into several possibilities: (1) indwelling (hulul) or union (ittihad); (2) concerning God's essence or attributes; (3) concerning Jesus' spirit or body; (4) other views like granting power to create or knowledge of the unseen, or honorary son-ship like Abraham's khilla. He then argues specifically against indwelling. If God indwells, it must be either by necessity (wujub) or by possibility (jawaz). The first is false for two reasons: (a) it would require either that the indweller is temporal (hadith) or the locus is eternal (qadim), both impossible for God; (b) necessary indwelling makes God dependent (muftaqir) on the locus, and whatever is dependent is contingent (mumkin bi al-dhat), contradicting divine necessity. The second possibility (indwelling by possibility) is also false because the very concept of indwelling requires the indweller to be dependent and in need of the locus; if that is lacking, it is not real indwelling. Finally, an objection is raised: why not say that God's essence necessitates indwelling conditionally upon the presence of the locus? The answer begins: we do not accept (la nusallim), and suggests that this conditional aspect still implies dependence, but the text cuts off. This refutes the Christian notion of hulul definitively.

Key Terms
حلول
اتحاد
ذات
صفة
تشريف
روح عيسى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Many people think Christians only believe in one kind of indwelling (like God literally entering Jesus' body), but Razi shows there are multiple nuanced positions.
Correction: Razi's classification reveals that Christian views range from indwelling of essence or attribute to union, and even to honorary status. Each must be addressed separately.

Checkpoint
According to Imam Razi, which of the following is NOT one of the possibilities he mentions in Christian speech?
A) Indwelling of God's essence in Jesus' spirit.
B) Indwelling of an attribute in Jesus' body.
C) Union of God's essence with Jesus' spirit.
D) That Jesus is God incarnate.

Key Takeaway
Imam Razi's classification shows that Christian claims about God's relation to Jesus are varied, but all fall into a few precise categories, each subject to rational refutation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a belief that seems confused, do you take the time to classify and understand it before rejecting it? What does Razi's method teach you about your own approach to error?
?
Razi asserts that it is impossible for God's essence to indwell in anything. Is there any way in which you have unconsciously limited God by imagining Him contained in a place, object, or even a person? How does this lesson confront that tendency?
?
The Christians are said to have 'extremely confused speech.' Where in your own understanding of God might there be confusion that needs precise classification? Are you willing to submit your assumptions to rigorous rational examination?

Refutation of Indwelling by Necessity
Razi refutes the possibility of hulul by necessity with two arguments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Imam Razi's two arguments against the idea that God necessarily indwells in something, and why such indwelling is impossible for the Necessary Being.

Core Idea
If God indwells by necessity, He becomes dependent, which contradicts His necessity.

Having classified Christian views, Imam Razi now begins his refutation. He first considers the possibility that God indwells by necessity (wujub). He gives two decisive arguments: one based on the temporal/eternal incompatibility, and another based on dependence (iftiqar). This passage presents those arguments.

Guided Path
1
Read the refutation passage
Read the Arabic passage from 'ونقول : أما القول بالحلول فهو باطل' up to 'والمفتقر إلى الغير ممكن بالذات'. Then read the translation. Note how Razi breaks the case into two divisions: hulul with necessity and with possibility.
This is a deductive argument: if hulul, then either with wujub or jawaz. He refutes both.
2
Understand the first argument
The first argument against necessary indwelling: If God indwells necessarily, then either the indweller (God) becomes temporal or the locus (e.g., Jesus' body) becomes eternal. Both are impossible. Why? Because if the indwelling relation is necessary, the indweller must exist in time if the locus is temporal, or the locus must be eternal if the indweller is eternal.
This argument relies on the incompatibility of temporal and eternal in the same relation.
3
Understand the second argument
The second argument: If God indwells necessarily, His essence becomes dependent on the locus. Anything dependent on something else is contingent (mumkin bi al-dhat), not necessary. Since God is necessary, this is impossible.
This is a classic argument from asma' wa sifat: necessity (wujub) precludes any need for another.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

What is the second reason Imam Razi gives against necessary indwelling?
A) It requires the indweller to be temporal.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You claim that God is completely independent, but is there a part of your life where you act as if your obedience earns His favor or presence? This lesson shows that nothing can contain God or make Him dependent. How will you uproot that subtle sense of entitlement today?
?
When you feel distant from God, do you try to 'bring Him down' through rituals or emotions, as if He needs a container? This refutation of hulul reminds you that God is above being confined by your efforts. What specific practice can you adopt to seek Him as the Transcendent One, not as someone who indwells your experiences?
?
If God's essence cannot depend on any created thing, then your sins cannot affect His essence, and your worship cannot benefit Him. So why do you do good deeds? Is it to meet your own need to feel close, or is it truly for His sake alone? Ponder this until you feel the weight of His independence.
